### NORMALIZED CONTENT

###### SysML v2 Plugin

Released on:July 18, 2025

The SysML v2 Alpha 1.8 release allows you to explore and evaluate the SysML v2 features implemented to date.

**[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Alpha 1.8 Version News' space='UAF2P']**

**[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Alpha 1.8 Version News' space='UAF2P']**

### SysML v2 Features

##### Model-Based Tabular Views & Columns

###### Model-Based Tabular Views

You can now model custom tabular views as part of your projects. You can either model custom tabular view definitions with custom-modeled columns from scratch or reuse predefined tabular view definitions and customize them according to your preferences. This enables greater flexibility in views modeling, allowing tabular views to be adapted to your specific needs while remaining an integral part of the model. Learn more [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Custom tabular view definitions' space='UAF2P']>]]> and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating custom tabular view definitions' space='UAF2P']>]]>

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Example of (1) predefined tabular view *Generic Table*, (2) customized *Generic Table* with the *Owned Element* columns removed, (3) custom *Drone Variant Table* with custom columns.

###### Table Column Modeling

Currently, two kinds of table columns are available for modeling:

- 
  - *ColumnByFeatureView*- for simple metadata feature value retrieval.
  - *ColumnByExpressionView*- for more complex metadata feature value retrieval.

The columns you create for a tabular view usage or definition must be defined by one of these column definitions, depending on the column's intended purpose. You can model custom columns for individual view usages as well as view definitions. This distinction supports both straightforward data display and more sophisticated modeling needs, enabling you to represent information in the table with the level of detail your project requires. Learn more [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Tabular view columns' space='UAF2P']>]]> and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Modeling tabular view columns' space='UAF2P']> ]]>

Using *ColumnByFeatureView* to model the *Owner* column:

view'Drone Requirements Table':'Requirements Table'{ 
exposeDroneStakeholderRequirements::**; 
renderrendering:>>asTable{ 
view:>>'Declared Name'; 
view:>>'Req Id'; 
view:>>Documentation;

// Using ColumnByFeatureView to model the Owner column:

viewOwner:ColumnByFeatureView:>column{ 
refitem:>>columnFeature=ownermetaFeature; 
} 
} 
}

*[IMAGE alt='' src='']*

Using *ColumnByExpressionView*to model the custom column *Weight*:

viewdef<vt>VariantTable:>'Base Table',NonStandardLibraryElementFilter{ 
filter@PartDefinitionor@PartUsage; 
renderrendering:>>asTable{ 
view:ColumnByFeatureView:>column{...}

// Using ColumnByExpressionView to model the custom column Weight: 
 
viewWeight:ColumnByExpressionView:> column { 
renderrenderingasTableCell:RealCellRendering:>asTableCell{ 
calc:>>getValue{ 
in:>>rowElement:Element; 
ifgetWeight(rowElement) @LiteralInteger? (getWeight(rowElement)asLiteralInteger).valueelse 
(getWeight(rowElement)asLiteralRational).value 
} 
calcgetWeight{ 
ine:Element; 
(((e.ownedElementasAttributeUsage)->ControlFunctions::select{ 
inee; 
(eeasElement).name=="weight" 
}asAttributeUsage).ownedRelationshipasFeatureValue).value 
} 
} 
} 
viewPrice:ColumnByExpressionView:> column {...} 
view'Net Price':ColumnByExpressionView:> column {...} 
} 
} 
view'Drone Variant Table':VariantTable{ 
filter@PartDefinitionandDefinition::isVariation; 
exposeDroneVariants::**; 
}

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Other Model-Based Tabular Views & Columns Improvements

- 
  - A new toolbar button has been added to tabular views, allowing you to open the current table view directly in the Textual Editor.
  - The isMultiline attribute has been introduced for single-valued string cells, enabling text wrapping and multiline display. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Modeling tabular view columns' space='UAF2P']>]]>
  - Editing of primitive ColumnByFeatureView cell values ( e.g., String, Element, Enum, Integer, Real, Boolean ) is now supported directly within the graphical representation of the table view.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### The **Open in Textual Editor**button; editing of the String value in a cell of the *Declared Name* column; text wrapping in the *Qualified Name*column cells via the *isMultiline*attribute.

##### View Creation Dialog Customization

###### Model-Based View Creation Dialog

You can now model a custom, model-based View Creation dialog that lists only the view creation commandsof your choice.

There are two options for customizing the View Creation dialog:

- 
  - Customize the predefined *SysMLViewCreationDialog*configuration in the *SysML Customization* model library. This allows you to inherit its configuration and tailor the View Creation dialog as needed. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Customizing View Creation dialog' space='UAF2P']>]]>
  - Create a View Creation dialog from scratch via the conceptual *ViewCreationDialog*definition. This gives you full control of designing the dialog entirely according to your own needs — without relying on predefined settings. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating View Creation dialog' space='UAF2P']>]]>

With either approach, you can define a model-based View Creation dialog that includes only the commands you need, as well as specifying how they are structured into custom command categories. This enables full customization of the dialog to match the needs of your specific project. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Custom View Creation dialog' space='UAF2P']>]]>

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### The image on the left shows the View Creation submenu according to the predefined *SysMLViewCreationDialog* configuration. The image on the right shows the customized View Creation submenu.

###### View Creation Dialog Management

Additionally, you can activate different View Creation dialog configurations for your project via the **Active Create View Dialog**. Use the **Manage Create View Dialog** command from the configuration element shortcut menu or the **Active View Creation Dialog** project option. While the predefined *SysMLViewCreationDialog* configuration is enabled by default for all SysML v2 projects, you can easily activate another configuration. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Activating View Creation dialog' space='UAF2P']>]]>

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### The **Manage Create View Dialog** command invokes the **Active Create View Dialog**, where the custom View Creation dialog's *CustomViewCreationDialog*configuration is activated for the project.

##### Cross Features Support

Cross features are now supported in the modeling tool, allowing you tospecify that a value at one end of the connection is linked to a value at the other end. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Cross features' space='UAF2P']>]]>

- You can specify cross features for connection ends as owned cross features or declare them in the related types of the connection using the cross subsetting relationship. Owned cross features can be named or unnamed. Cross features in connection usages support both full and shorthand notations.

/* cross features owned by the connection definition ends */ 
partdefHub; 
partdefDevice; 
connectiondefDeviceConnection{ 
end[0..1]parthub:Hub; 
end[1..*]orderedpartdevice:Device; 
} 
partdefNetworkConfiguration{ 
partnetworkHubs:Hub[*]; 
partnetworkDevices:Device[*]; 
connectionnetworkConnections:DeviceConnection{ 
end[1]parthub::>networkHubs; 
end[0..4]orderedpartdevice::>networkDevices; 
} 
}

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

- Additionally, Move Cross Feature to End and Move Cross Feature to End Type refactoring commands are available for connection definition ends, allowing you to convert ends between the two declaration options.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

##### SysML v1 to SysML v2 Migration Progress

- The SysML v1 to SysML v2 Migration plugin has been enhanced, now supporting a broader range of elements. However, as the plugin is still a work in progress, not all SysML v1 elements are currently supported for migration. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Migration from SysML v1 to SysML v2' space='UAF2P']>]]>

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### A SysML v1 model and its result after migration to SysML v2.

- Additionally, if the migration includes any failures, a .*xlsx* migration status file is now generated. This file lists separate sheets for elements and properties that were not migrated. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Migration from SysML v1 to SysML v2' space='UAF2P']>]]>

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

##### Style Sheet Improvements

###### Style Sheet Management Improvements

- You can now activate style sheets for both the entire project and for individual views. This flexibility allows you to combine multiple style sheets based on your modeling needs (for example, activating a style sheet for the entire project while activating distinct style sheets for individual views). Additionally, style sheets activated at both the project and view levels can be prioritized by setting their order of application. You can activate style sheets either via the Textual Editor or using the newly introduced **Style Sheets** button in the view toolbar. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P']>]]>

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### The *DefaultStyleSheet*is activated for the entire project via the **Style Sheets**button in the view toolbar, while the *NewStyle***style sheet, which changes the color of an interface usage, is activated for the specific view *vehicle*.

- You can also disable project-level style sheets for a specific view. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P']>]]>

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Disabling active project style sheets for the *vehicle*view via the **Apply Style Sheet**dialog.

###### Other Style Sheet Improvements

- A new rule condition, *FreeFormCondition,*has been introduced for style sheet rules, allowing you to target element symbols by the specified expression. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P']>]]>
- Style sheet part definitions can now be displayed as symbols in views, featuring a dedicated compartment that lists their rules—each accompanied by an icon that visually reflects the defined style. [ATTACHMENT filename='defaultstylesheetpartdefinition.png']

##### Semantic and Non-Semantic Metadata Representation

As two kinds of metadata can be applied to model elements—semantic and non-semantic—representational differences have been implemented in accordance with the SysML v2 language specification. The following differences apply to element representation in the Containment tree, Specification panel, symbols on views, and any other UI instances. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Metadata' space='UAF2P']>]]>

If an element has at least one semantic metadata applied to it:

- The element's metaclass keyword (e.g., part ) is not displayed.
- The applied semantic metadata name is displayed with the # sign within guillemets « ». The def keyword is appended for definition elements. [ATTACHMENT filename='semantic_metadata.png']

If an element has only non-semantic metadata applied to it:

- The applied semantic metadata name is not displayed; thus, element representation remains essentially unchanged. The element only displays metadata-related information in the metadata compartment and a metadata annotation. [ATTACHMENT filename='non-semantic_metadata.png']

##### Package Member Display

This release introduces display options for package members, providing you with greater control and visibility.

- The new Display Owned Members and Display Owned Members Recursively commands allow you to view package members in both Nested-view and Tree-view styles. [ATTACHMENT filename='Display Owned Members commands.png']
- The package element symbol now supports displaying its members directly within the members compartment, improving the visibility of the package structure. [ATTACHMENT filename='Members compartment.png']
- A new symbol property, Show Only Owned, has been added for the members compartment. It allows you to choose whether to display only the elements owned by the package or include the imported ones as well. [ATTACHMENT filename='Show only owned symbol property.png']

##### Graphical Notation Improvements for Loop and If-Else Action Usages

This release introduces several graphical notation enhancements for *for loops*, *while loops*, and *if-else actions*, improving clarity and visual consistency:

- Action conditions — such as if , while , until , and loop iterators — are now shown in dedicated compartments, rather than within the name header.
- Nested actions are now displayed in graphical compartments, instead of being listed under body, thenClause , or elseClause .
- As a result, Tree-view style display commands now display nested elements in a Nested-view style within their respective compartments.

###### [IMAGE alt='' src='']The *if* action with the *if condition*compartment as well as nested actions in *thenClause* and *elseClause*compartments.

##### Navigation for Elements Connected via Interfaces

The Go To commandnow supports navigation between elements connected through their owned or inherited ports via interfaces.[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Element navigation' space='UAF2P']>]]>

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

##### Specification Panel and Window Improvements

###### Context-Aware Inherited Features

To prevent unintended global model changes, clicking the Navigate button next to an inherited feature now opens that feature in the Specification panel in read-only mode. If you need to modify the default value in the current context, you can click the Redefine button to redefine the feature. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification panel' space='UAF2P']>]]>

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Toggle Library Elements' Visibility in the Specification Window

You can now choose to display library elements for properties in the Specification window, providing a more comprehensive view of model elements. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='UAF2P']>]]>

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Other Specification Panel and Window Improvements

- 
  - Holding down the CTRL key while dragging and dropping elements onto element-typed fields in the Specification panel (e.g., Type, Use Case Included, etc.) now allows you to add the dropped element in addition to the set element.
  - The issue where it was possible to change Declared Name, Short Name, Documentation for elements that cannot have those properties (e.g., specializations) has been fixed.

##### Other Improvements

- The View Properties dialog has been introduced, which can be invoked via the View Properties command in the view's shortcut menu. It contains the Use Gradient Fill style property allowing you to specify whether a gradient should be used for the Fill Color and Content Fill Color symbol style properties. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Modifying styles of individual views' space='UAF2P']>]]>
- New symbol properties have been introduced:
  - The Show Name symbol property, allowing you to choose whether the element name should be displayed on the element symbol. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Modifying styles of individual symbols' space='UAF2P']>]]>
  - The Show Short Name symbol property, allowing you to choose whether the element short name should be displayed on the element symbol. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Modifying styles of individual symbols' space='UAF2P']>]]>
  - The Show Only Owned symbol property, allowing you to specify whether only the owned elements or imported ones, too, should be displayed in the symbol compartment. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Modifying styles of individual symbols' space='UAF2P']>]]>
  - The Show Modifiers symbol property, allowing you to specify whether the element's modifiers (e.g., *in, ref, abstract*, etc.) should be displayed on the element symbol. The property does not control the individual and portion kind (timeslice, snapshot) modifiers. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Modifying styles of individual symbols' space='UAF2P']>]]>
  - The Text Vertical Position symbol property, allowing you to specify the element name position for the symbol. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Modifying styles of individual symbols' space='UAF2P']>]]>

**Documentation**

- SysML v2 Alpha 1.8
- SysML v2 Evaluation Alpha 1.8
- SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling 1.8

ac:type="single"><ac:layout-cell><h1>SysML v2 Features</h1><h3><span>Model-Based Tabular Views &amp; Columns </span></h3><h4 style="margin-left: 40.0px;"><span>Model-Based Tabular Views</span></h4><p You can model custom columns for individual view usages as well as view definitions. This distinction supports both straightforward data display and more sophisticated modeling needs, enabling you to represent information in the table with the level of detail your project requires. Learn more <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Tabular view columns" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[here >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> and <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Modeling tabular view columns" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[ here >> ]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> <br /><br /></span></p></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="two_equal"><ac:layout-cell><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-green-bolder,#164b35);">Using <em>ColumnByFeatureView</em> to model the <em>Owner</em> column:</span></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="panel" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="894ecc7b-12bc-481d-b14e-167c227aa3bf"><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">view</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">'Drone Requirements Table'</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> : </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-teal,#206a83);">'Requirements Table'</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> {</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">    </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">expose</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-teal,#206a83);">DroneStakeholderRequirements</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">::**;</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">    </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">render</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">rendering</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> :&gt;&gt; ri:filename="modeling_ColumnByExpressionView.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="single"><ac:layout-cell><h4>Other Model-Based Tabular Views &amp; Columns Improvements</h4><ul><li style="list-style-type: none;"><ul><li data-uuid="329559b4-0197-4e07-b9ea-a2d0b878499f">A new toolbar button has been added to tabular views, allowing you to open the current table view directly in the Textual Editor.</li><li data-uuid="192ea281-7975-4712-bbc3-b8990c7a0b79">The <em>isMultiline</em> attribute has been introduced for single-valued string cells, enabling text wrapping and multiline display. <ac:link ac:anchor="Modifying table column attributes"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Modeling tabular view columns" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></li><li data-uuid="556ecce7-2ea1-415d-a661-a5fa45b94c84">Editing of primitive <em>ColumnByFeatureView</em> cell values (<ac:inline-comment-marker ac:ref="60858666-bb50-4245-9efe-c9b897380295">e.g., String, Element, Enum, Integer, Real, Boolean</ac:inline-comment-marker>) is now supported directly within the graphical representation of the table view.</li></ul></li></ul><p><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="Other Model-Based Tabular Views &amp; Columns Improvements.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><h6 style="text-align: center;">The <strong>Open in Textual Editor </strong>button; editing of the String value in a cell of the <em>Declared Name</em> column; text wrapping in the <em>Qualified Name </em>column cells via the <em>isMultiline </em>attribute.</h6><h3>View Creation Dialog Customization</h3><h4 style="margin-left: 40.0px;">Model-Based View Creation Dialog</h4><p style="margin-left: 40.0px;"><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">You can now model a custom, model-based View Creation dialog that lists only the view creation commands</span><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;"> of your choice.</span></p><p style="margin-left: 40.0px;">There are two options for customizing the View Creation dialog:</p><ul><li style="list-style-type: none;" data-uuid="9a827616-2ee3-4119-8eea-78035a5be441"><ul><li data-uuid="a9d61dda-14de-44ab-ba8c-c6368461717e"><p>Customize the predefined <em style="text-align: left;">SysMLViewCreationDialog </em>configuration in the <em>SysML Customization</em> model library. This allows you to inherit its configuration and tailor the View Creation dialog as needed. <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Customizing View Creation dialog" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></p></li><li data-uuid="c039f97c-ce22-4e86-a073-6241b54caf06"><p>Create a View Creation dialog from scratch <span>via the conceptual <em>ViewCreationDialog </em>definition</span>. This gives you full control of designing the dialog entirely according to your own needs — without relying on predefined settings. <span><ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Creating View Creation dialog" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span></p></li></ul></li></ul><p style="margin-left: 40.0px;">With either approach, you can define a model-based View Creation dialog that includes only the commands you need, as well as specifying how they are structured into custom command categories. This enables full customization of the dialog to match the needs of your specific project. <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Custom View Creation dialog" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></p><p style="text-align: center;"><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="Model-Based View Creation Dialog.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><h6 style="text-align: center;">The image on the left shows the View Creation submenu according to the predefined <em>SysMLViewCreationDialog</em> configuration. The image on the right shows the customized View Creation submenu.  </h6><h4 style="margin-left: 40.0px;">View Creation Dialog Management</h4><p style="margin-left: 40.0px;">Additionally, you can activate different View Creation dialog configurations for your project via the <strong>Active Create View Dialog</strong>. Use the <strong>Manage Create View Dialog</strong> command from the configuration element shortcut menu or the <strong>Active View Creation Dialog</strong> project option. While the predefined <em style="text-align: left;">SysMLViewCreationDialog</em> configuration is enabled by default for all SysML v2 projects, you can easily activate another configuration. <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Activating View Creation dialog" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></p><p style="margin-left: 40.0px;text-align: center;"><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="View Creation Dialog Management.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><h6 style="margin-left: 40.0px;text-align: center;">The <strong>Manage Create View Dialog</strong> command invokes the <strong>Active Create View Dialog</strong>, where the custom View Creation dialog's <em>CustomViewCreationDialog </em>configuration is activated for the project.</h6><h3 style="text-align: left;">Cross Features Support</h3><p><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">Cross features are now supported in the modeling tool, allowing you to </span><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">specify that a value at one end of the connection is linked to a value at the other end. <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Cross features" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span></p><ul><li><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">You can specify cross features for connection ends as owned cross features or declare them in the related types of the connection using the cross subsetting relationship. Owned cross features can be named or unnamed. Cross features in connection usages support both full and shorthand notations.</span> </li></ul></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="two_equal"><ac:layout-cell><ac:structured-macro ac:name="panel" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="9c4c3354-4a75-4b25-899d-b9b6745028ff"><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-green-bolder,#164b35);">/* cross features owned by the connection definition ends */</span><br /><span /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">}</span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:layout-cell><ac:layout-cell><p><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="cross_feature_support.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><p><br /></p></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="single"><ac:layout-cell><ul><li data-uuid="2598a84c-b7ba-41ce-af4e-52ccedb36012">Additionally, <strong>Move Cross Feature to End </strong>and <strong>Move Cross Feature to End Type </strong>refactoring commands are available for connection definition ends, allowing you to convert ends between the two declaration options.</li></ul><p><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="cross_features_refactoring.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="single"><ac:layout-cell><h3 style="text-align: left;">SysML v1 to SysML v2 Migration Progress</h3><ul><li data-uuid="98c98c20-66d0-456d-ae10-ed24c75b1d34">The <strong>SysML v1 to SysML v2 Migration</strong> plugin has been enhanced, now supporting a broader range of elements. However, as the plugin is still a work in progress, not all SysML v1 elements are currently supported for migration. <span><ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Migration from SysML v1 to SysML v2" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span></li></ul><p><span><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="SysML v1 to SysML v2 Migration Progress.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></span></p><h6 style="text-align: center;">A SysML v1 model and its result after migration to SysML v2.</h6><ul><li data-uuid="7b5002e5-3de8-4891-8b47-beed6f5c6382"><span>Additionally, if the migration includes any failures, a .<em>xlsx</em> migration status file is now generated. This file lists separate sheets for elements and properties that were not migrated. <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Migration from SysML v1 to SysML v2" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span></li></ul><p><span><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="SysML v1 to SysML v2 Migration.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></span></p></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="single"><ac:layout-cell><h3>Style Sheet Improvements</h3><h4>Style Sheet Management Improvements</h4><ul><li data-uuid="0e45ebf8-ad33-47f7-88c2-39e822040fd3">You can now activate style sheets for both the entire project and for individual views. <span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">This flexibility allows you to combine multiple style sheets based on your modeling needs (for example, activating a style sheet for the entire project while activating distinct style sheets for individual views). Additionally, style sheets activated at both the project and view levels can be prioritized by setting their order of application. You can activate style sheets either via the Textual Editor or using the newly introduced <strong>Style Sheets</strong> button in the view toolbar. <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Activating style sheets" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span></li></ul><p style="text-align: center;"><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="Style Sheet Improvements 1.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><h6 style="text-align: center;">The <em>DefaultStyleSheet </em>is activated for the entire project via the <strong>Style Sheets </strong>button in the view toolbar, while the <em>NewStyle</em><em> </em>style sheet, which changes the color of an interface usage, is activated for the specific view <em>vehicle</em>. </h6><ul><li data-uuid="38e55d56-b392-4c1e-ac26-bfaeb390b7d5"><span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">You can also disable project-level style sheets for a specific view.</span> <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Activating style sheets" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span></li></ul><p style="text-align: center;"><span><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="Style Sheet Improvements 2.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></span></p><h6 style="text-align: center;"><span>Disabling active project style sheets for the <em>vehicle </em>view via the <strong>Apply Style Sheet </strong>dialog.</span></h6><h4>Other Style Sheet Improvements</h4><ul><li style="text-align: left;"><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">A new rule condition, <em>FreeFormCondition, </em>has been introduced for style sheet rules, allowing you to target element symbols by the specified expression. <ac:link ac:anchor="Specifying conditions for a rule"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Creating style sheet components" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span></li><li style="text-align: left;">Style sheet part definitions can now be displayed as symbols in views, featuring a dedicated compartment that lists their rules—each accompanied by an icon that visually reflects the defined style.<br /> <ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="defaultstylesheetpartdefinition.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></li></ul></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="single"><ac:layout-cell><h3>Semantic and Non-Semantic Metadata Representation</h3><p>As two kinds of metadata can be applied to model elements—semantic and non-semantic—representational differences have been implemented in accordance with the SysML v2 language specification. The following differences apply to element representation <span>in the Containment tree, Specification panel, symbols on views, and any other UI instances. <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Metadata" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span></p></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="two_equal"><ac:layout-cell><p>If an element has at least one semantic metadata applied to it:</p><ul><li data-uuid="df0a688c-b0e0-4f5f-8cfd-01f38031f884">The element's metaclass keyword (e.g., <em>part</em>) is not displayed.</li><li data-uuid="ddc87aa6-65d0-4b68-ba3b-5f3fea0ba123">The applied semantic metadata name is displayed with the # sign within guillemets « ». The <em>def</em> keyword is appended for definition elements. <br /><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="semantic_metadata.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></li></ul></ac:layout-cell><ac:layout-cell><p>If an element has only non-semantic metadata applied to it:</p><ul><li data-uuid="7d37d4c1-8a75-476d-8331-f69f1276a880">The applied semantic metadata name is not displayed; thus, element representation remains essentially unchanged. The element only displays metadata-related information in the metadata compartment and a metadata annotation. <br /><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="non-semantic_metadata.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></li></ul></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="single"><ac:layout-cell><h3>Package Member Display</h3><p><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">This release introduces display options for package members, providing you with greater control and visibility. </span></p><ul><li data-uuid="7c082775-8f44-470f-96b6-aac62aab1701"><p>The new Display Owned Members and Display Owned Members Recursively commands allow you to view package members in both Nested-view and Tree-view styles.</p><br /><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="Display Owned Members commands.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></li><li data-uuid="f31b2650-91c3-4059-a5e3-83ae0f14b530"><p>The package element symbol now supports displaying its members directly within the members compartment, improving the visibility of the package structure.</p><br /><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="Members compartment.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></li><li data-uuid="f6727132-78d8-482f-bcb2-8141e6d76ab4"><p>A new symbol property, Show Only Owned, has been added for the members compartment. It allows you to choose whether to display only the elements owned by the package or include the imported ones as well.</p><br /><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="Show only owned symbol property.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></li></ul><p><br /></p><h3>Graphical Notation Improvements for Loop and If-Else Action Usages</h3><p><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">This release introduces several graphical notation enhancements for <em>for loops</em>, <em>while loops</em>, and <em>if-else actions</em>, improving clarity and visual consistency:</span></p><ul><li data-uuid="2ad9ce6d-b4e8-425e-864e-9c28e5b76bf3">Action conditions — such as <em>if</em>, <em>while</em>, <em>until</em>, and <em>loop </em>iterators — are now shown in dedicated compartments, rather than within the name header.</li><li data-uuid="5b6510fd-6c8c-4808-b6c5-8b0ed2126587">Nested actions are now displayed in graphical compartments, instead of being listed under body, <em>thenClause</em>, or <em>elseClause</em>.</li><li data-uuid="704b4356-2ec8-4437-afad-6bb6b69a6805">As a result, Tree-view style display commands now display nested elements in a Nested-view style within their respective compartments.</li></ul><h6 style="text-align: center;"><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="Graphical Notation Improvements for Loop and If-Else Action Usages.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image>The <em>if</em> action with the <em>if condition </em>compartment as well as nested actions in <em>thenClause</em> and <em>elseClause </em>compartments.</h6><h3>Navigation for Elements Connected via Interfaces</h3><p><ac:inline-comment-marker ac:ref="5dd01ef3-3bc0-44c7-abb7-9a1adfdc035a">The Go To command</ac:inline-comment-marker><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;"> now supports navigation between elements connected through their owned or inherited ports via interfac</span><ac:inline-comment-marker ac:ref="166d9ff3-0d9d-4fc5-919b-5616531fd446">es</ac:inline-comment-marker><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">. </span><ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Element navigation" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></p><p><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="Navigation for Elements Connected via Interfaces.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="single"><ac:layout-cell><h3>Specification Panel and Window Improvements</h3><h4>Context-Aware Inherited Features</h4><p>To prevent unintended global model changes, clicking the Navigate button next to an inherited feature now opens that feature in the Specification panel in read-only mode. If you need to modify the default value in the current context, you can click the Redefine button to redefine the feature. <ac:link ac:anchor="Redefining inherited features via the compartment in the Specification panel"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Specification panel" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></p><p><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="Context-Aware Inherited Features.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><h4>Toggle Library Elements' Visibility in the Specification Window</h4><p>You can now choose to display library elements for properties in the Specification window, providing a more comprehensive view of model elements. <ac:link ac:anchor="Toggling library elements' visibility in the Specification Window"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Specification window" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></p><p><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="Toggle Library Elements Visibility in the Specification Window.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Alpha 1.8 Version News" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><h4>Other Specification Panel and Window Improvements</h4><ul><li style="list-style-type: none;" data-uuid="f0542a8d-5c9d-4348-9325-8f3cf108f304"><ul><li>Holding down the CTRL key while dragging and dropping elements onto element-typed fields in the Specification panel (e.g., Type, Use Case Included, etc.) now allows you to add the dropped element in addition to the set element.</li><li>The issue where it was possible to change Declared Name, Short Name, Documentation for elements that cannot have those properties (e.g., specializations) has been fixed.</li></ul></li></ul><h3><span>Other Improvements</span></h3><ul><li><span>The View Properties dialog has been introduced, which can be invoked via the View Properties command in the view's shortcut menu. It contains the Use Gradient Fill style property allowing you to specify whether a gradient should be used for the Fill Color and Content Fill Color symbol style properties. <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Modifying styles of individual views" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span></li><li data-uuid="55c48910-40e2-4952-9f61-2423ce315e46"><span>New symbol properties have been introduced:</span><ul><li><span>The Show Name symbol property, allowing you to choose whether the element name should be displayed on the element symbol. <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Modifying styles of individual symbols" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span></li><li data-uuid="751592c7-d996-4674-8e95-baa9129a734c"><span>The Show Short Name symbol property, allowing you to choose whether the element short name should be displayed on the element symbol. <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Modifying styles of individual symbols" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span></li><li data-uuid="f2e99d35-009d-472e-ad7f-5787135b7ac5">The Show Only Owned <span>symbol property, allowing you to specify whether only the owned elements or imported ones, too, should be displayed in the symbol compartment. <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Modifying styles of individual symbols" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span></li><li data-uuid="c1d16afc-d055-4de3-84c9-5a04315f1e1f">The Show Modifiers <span>symbol property, allowing you to specify whether the element's modifiers (e.g., <em>in, ref, abstract</em>, etc.) should be displayed on the element symbol. The property does not control the individual and portion kind (timeslice, snapshot) modifiers. <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Modifying styles of individual symbols" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span></li><li data-uuid="72563b93-9b69-4f5e-b1bb-763be0e0755f">The Text Vertical Position symbol property, allowing you to specify the element name position for the symbol. <span><ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Modifying styles of individual symbols" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Learn more >>]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span></li></ul></li></ul></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="single"><ac:layout-cell><p><br /></p><hr /></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="single"><ac:layout-cell><p><strong>Documentation</strong></p><ul><li data-uuid="7d7103ec-d2b6-400e-b65a-e5ec02953fe4">SysML v2 Alpha 1.8</li><li data-uuid="6253c926-2ba3-43c0-b1e9-f5d5dfca484e">SysML v2 Evaluation Alpha 1.8</li><li data-uuid="83416f29-8151-4282-93e9-797c4a7228a4">SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling 1.8</li></ul></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section></ac:layout>

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=298090625 space=UAF2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 00206: COPY Activating style sheets

- page_id: `298090625`
- space_key: `UAF2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UAF2P/pages/298090625/COPY+Activating+style+sheets
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-03-26T12:07:27.303+01:00`
- ancestors: COPY Symbol styles
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

Whether you're using predefined style sheets provided by the modeling tool or custom ones you've created, you can manage which style sheets are activated for the entire project and which for specific views. This flexibility allows you to combine multiple style sheets based on your modeling needs, for example, activating a global style sheet for the entire project while activating distinct style sheets for individual views. Additionally, style sheets activated at both the project and view levels can be prioritized by setting their order of application. You can also disable project-level style sheets for a specific view.

Style sheets can be activated for:

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P']

##### Style sheets activation priority order

The order of priority in which the style sheets are activated for views:

1. The configurations for activating style sheets for individual views are of the highest priority. They are always of higher priority than the configuration for activating style sheets for the entire project.
  1. Take note of the type of style sheets you are using, i.e., whether [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] or [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheets' space='UAF2P']. Those that reuse another style sheet inherit the latter's rules. This can result in unexpected usage of styles even if their style sheets are not activated directly. ExampleYou have a custom style sheet, *NewStyleSheet**,* which is created by subclassifying the *DefaultStyleSheet*. The *NewStyleSheet*contains several rules slightly modifying the *DefaultStyleSheet.*You activate *NewStyleSheet*for a specific view and *BlackAndWhiteStyleSheet* for the entire project.The specific view with the activated *NewStyleSheet*displays some symbols with the styles inherited from the *DefaultStyleSheet*, even though the latter is not activated for the project.
2. The ordering of style sheets for both individual views and the entire project is taken into account. If you specify multiple style sheets, order them based on your preferred priority, as the style sheets higher on the list take precedence over those lower on the list. Activating multiple style sheets is useful if the prioritized style sheet does not cover all available symbols. In that case, the secondary style sheet will cover those not covered by the first (if it contains the necessary rules).
3. The configuration for activating style sheets for the entire project is considered last.

##### Activating style sheets for the project

There must always be at least one style sheet activated for the project. If no style sheet is activated by the user, the default active project style sheet is *DefaultStyleSheet*.

###### Activating style sheets for the project via the Textual Editor

To activate style sheets for the project via the Textual Editor

1. Do one of the following:
  1. If the model already contains the root namespace dedicated to configurations that activate style sheets and creation dialogs, open it in the Textual Editor.
  2. If the model does not contain this namespace, [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Managing elements' space='UAF2P'] and open it in the Textual Editor.
2. In the root namespace, declare a package named ProjectStyleConfig .
3. In the package's body, declare a part definition named myProjectStyleConfig and subset DS_Styles::CoreStylesComponents::StyleConfiguration .
4. In the part definition's body, declare a part and define it by the part definition of the style sheet you want to activate for the project, then subset activeStyleSheets .
5. Click the**Synchronize**button.

packageProjectStyleConfig{ 
partdefmyProjectStyleConfig:>DS_Styles::CoreStylesComponents::StyleConfiguration{ 
part:DS_Styles::StyleSheets::BlackAndWhiteStyleSheet:>activeStyleSheets; //*BlackAndWhiteStyleSheet* is activated for the project 
} 
}

###### Activating style sheets for the project via the Style Sheets button

To activate style sheets for the project via the Style Sheets button

1. Click the Style Sheets button in the view toolbar. In the dropdown menu, click Project Style Sheets command. The Project Style Sheets dialog opens.
2. On the left side panel of the **Project Style Sheets**dialog, select the style sheet(s) you want to use and click the **Add [IMAGE alt='' src='']**button.
3. Select a style sheet on the right side of the panel and click the **Up**or **Down**buttons to change the selected style sheet's priority.
4. Click the OK button. The selected style sheets are activated and element symbols are updated on project view s. Activating style sheets for the project via the **Style Sheets** button****automatically creates a new package *ProjectStyleConfig* with the active project style sheets configuration. The package is created in a root namespace dedicated to configurations that activate [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P'], [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Custom creation dialogs' space='UAF2P'], and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Enabling validation suites' space='UAF2P']. If no such namespace exists in the model, it is automatically created with the *ProjectStyleConfig*package. The root namespace's name depends on the name of the package first created in the namespace.The procedure [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] details the package's textual notation if you opt to create it manually.[IMAGE alt='' src='']

##### Activating style sheets for a specific view

To activate style sheets for a specific view, the view must be defined by a symbolic view definition.

- Symbolic views containing *Views::asInterconnectionDiagram* or *Views::asTreeDiagram* renderers, but [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating symbolic views' space='UAF2P'], are automatically defined by *DS_Views::SymbolicViews::gv* once you [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P'].
- If you are [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P'], you must first [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating symbolic views' space='UAF2P'], e.g., *DS_Views::SymbolicViews::gv.*

###### Activating style sheets for a specific view via the Textual Editor

To activate style sheets for a specific view via the Textual Editor

1. In the Textual Editor, p lace the cursor within the body of the specific view whose style sheets you want to modify.
2. Declare a part and define it by the needed style sheet, then subset *explicitlyAppliedStyleSheets*.
3. (Optional) To i gnore the specification of active project style sheets for the selected view, only taking into account the style sheets specified for this exact view:
  1. Declare a part, redefine *effectiveStyleSheets*and set it to *explicitlyAppliedStyleSheets*.
4. Click the**Synchronize**button.

view'General View':DS_Views::SymbolicViews::gv{

// ignores active project style sheets for the view, activating only those specified to be active for this view:part :>> effectiveStyleSheets = explicitlyAppliedStyleSheets;

// activating *NewStyle1*and *NewStyle2* style sheets for this specific view:

part:NewStylesPackage::NewStyle1:>explicitlyAppliedStyleSheets; 
part:NewStylesPackage::NewStyle2:>explicitlyAppliedStyleSheets;

// alternative notation for active style sheet specification for a specific view (equivalent to the above):

part:>>explicitlyAppliedStyleSheets= (NewStylesPackage::NewStyle1(),NewStylesPackage::NewStyle2()); 
}

###### Activating style sheets for a specific view via the Style Sheets button

To activate style sheets for a specific view via the Style Sheets button

1. Open the specific view whose style sheets you want to modify.
2. Click the Style Sheets button in the view toolbar . In the dropdown menu, click Apply Style Sheets command. The Apply Style Sheets dialog opens.
3. On the left side panel of the **Apply****Style Sheets**dialog, select the style sheet(s) you want to use and click the **Add [IMAGE alt='' src='']**button.
4. Select a style sheet on the right side of the panel and click the **Up**or **Down**buttons to change the selected style sheet's priority.
5. (Optional) Select the check box for the Ignore Active Project Style Sheets option. Selecting the option ignores the specification of active project style sheets specified in the **Project Style Sheets** dialog for the selected view, only taking into account the style sheets specified for this exact view in the **Apply** Style Sheets dialog .
6. Click the OK button. The selected style sheets are activated, and element symbols are updated in the view .

###### Displaying style sheets activated for a specific view

To display style sheets activated for a specific view

1. Open the specific view.
2. Click the Style Sheets button in the view toolbar . In the dropdown menu, click Display Applied Style Sheets command. Part definition element symbols of the style sheets activated for the view are displayed in the view. If style sheets are activated for the entire project, but none for the specific view, the command will not display the style sheet symbols.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=298090607 space=UAF2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 00207: COPY Creating style sheet components

- page_id: `298090607`
- space_key: `UAF2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UAF2P/pages/298090607/COPY+Creating+style+sheet+components
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-03-26T12:07:25.107+01:00`
- ancestors: COPY Symbol styles > COPY Custom style sheets
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

See the procedures on this page to create style sheet components.

#### Creating custom style sheet components

##### Creating global conditions for a style sheet

In addition to specifying conditions for individual rules in the style sheet (see procedure [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P']), you can specify a global condition that applies to the entire style sheet. All individual rules declared in the style sheet apply only to the symbols that comply with the global rule.

###### Creating global conditions for a style sheet

To create global conditions for a style sheet

1. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] .
2. Within the body of the part definition of the new style sheet, redefine the *styleSheetCondition*element inherited from the StyleSheet element and define it by the needed condition.
3. Within the body of the condition, declare a ref item , then r edefine the needed item and specify its values. The available ref items and their value types depend on the condition definition you are using. For a list of the condition definitions and their available ref items, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P']page.
4. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications' space='UAF2P']. // the following style sheet contains a global condition 'General View Condition' followed by an individual rule for a specific element metaclass and applicable stylepackageNewStylesPackage{privateimportDS_Styles::**;privateimportCoreStylesComponents::*; 
 privateimportPredicates::*; 
 privateimportColorDefinitions::*; 
 privateimportCompartmentVisibilityDefinitions::*; 
 privateimportKerMLStyles::*; 
 privateimportSysMLStyles::*; 
partdefNewStyleSheet:>StyleSheet{ 
/* -------global condition -------*/ 
part'General View Condition':>>styleSheetCondition:ByDiagramTypeCondition{ // global style sheet condition targeting symbols by view definition 
refitem:>>diagramType=DS_Views::SymbolicViews::gv.metadata; // the condition targets views defined by the *General View*view definition 
} 
/* -----------------------------------*/ 
partpartRule:>rule{ // an individual rule targets *PartUsage* metaclasses and applies the specified style to them. Because of the global rule, only part usages displayed on a General View will be affected by the rule 
part:>>condition:ByElementMetaclassCondition{ 
refitem:>>elementMetaclass= SysML::Systems::PartUsage.metadata; 
} 
view:ShapeStyle:>>style{ 
attribute:>>textColordefault"#2A16FF"; 
} 
} 
} 
}

##### Creating custom rules

###### Creating custom rules via the Textual Editor

To create a custom rule via the Textual Editor

1. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] .
2. Within the body of the part definition of the new style sheet, s pecify the rule, d eclare a part usage, specify a name for the new rule, subset the rule element inherited from the StyleSheet element, and in its body, do any of the following as needed:
  1. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] .
  2. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] .
3. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications' space='UAF2P']. packageNewStylesPackage{privateimportDS_Styles::**;privateimportCoreStylesComponents::*; 
 privateimportPredicates::*; 
 privateimportColorDefinitions::*; 
 privateimportCompartmentVisibilityDefinitions::*; 
 privateimportKerMLStyles::*; 
 privateimportSysMLStyles::*; 
partdefNewStyleSheet:> StyleSheet{/* -------new rule -------*/ 
partpartRule:>rule{// Specify the rule's condition 
 // Specify the rule's style 
}/* -----------------------------------*/ 
} 
}

###### Creating custom rules via the style sheet symbol compartment in a view

To create a custom rule via the style sheet symbol compartment in a view

1. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] .
2. Create the rule part usage element for the style sheet's part definition element via the Create Element button by following the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Compartments' space='UAF2P'] procedure. A rule is created with the ByElementCondition condition and ShapeStyle style, which includes redefinitions for fillColor (with a randomly assigned color value) and penColor (with a comparatively darker color value) attributes. You can modify them as needed, see [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] . 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']

partpart1:>rule{ 
part:>>condition:DS_Styles::CoreStylesComponents::Predicates::ByElementCondition; 
part:>>style:DS_Styles::CoreStylesComponents::KerMLStyles::ShapeStyle{ 
attribute:>>fillColor="#81c784"; 
attribute:>>penColor="#3e6140"; 
} 
}

###### Creating custom rules via the Specification panel

To create a custom rule via the Specification panel

1. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] .
2. Create the rule part usage element for the style sheet's part definition element via the Specification panel by following the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification panel' space='UAF2P'] procedure. A rule is created with the ByElementCondition (Specific Elements) condition and ShapeStyle style, which includes redefinitions for fillColor (with a randomly assigned color value) and penColor (with a comparatively darker color value) attributes. You can modify them as needed, see [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] . 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']

partpart1:>rule{ 
part:>>condition:DS_Styles::CoreStylesComponents::Predicates::ByElementCondition; 
part:>>style:DS_Styles::CoreStylesComponents::KerMLStyles::ShapeStyle{ 
attribute:>>fillColor="#81c784"; 
attribute:>>penColor="#3e6140"; 
} 
}

##### Specifying conditions for a rule

You can specify the condition for a rule via the Textual Editor or the Specification panel. The names of the conditions differ based on the chosen specification method. See the comparison table below.

| Condition Element Name in Textual Editor | Condition Name in Specification Panel |
| --- | --- |
| ByElementCondition | Specific Elements |
| ByElementMetaclassCondition | Element Kind |
| ByMetadataAnnotationCondition | Metadata Annotation |
| ByDiagramTypeCondition | View Type |
| FreeFormCondition | Custom Expression |

For more information, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P']page.

###### Specifying conditions for a rule via the Textual Editor

To specify a condition for a rule via the Textual Editor

1. Within the body of the part element of the rule, declare a part usage and r edefine the condition element inherited from the StyleSheet element, then define it by the needed condition.
2. Within the body of the condition, declare a ref item , then r edefine the needed item and specify its values.
  1. For the ByElementCondition , in its body, declare a ref item and redefine dependencyOwner . In its body, declare a [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Dependency' space='UAF2P'] from the rule's condition to the target element.
  2. For the FreeFormCondition , declare a calc and redefine test , then specify the needed expression. The available ref items and their value types depend on the condition definition you are using. For a list of the condition definitions and their available ref items, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P']page.
3. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications' space='UAF2P']. // *ByElementCondition* examplepartcustomRule:>rule{ 
part:>>condition:DS_Styles::CoreStylesComponents::Predicates::ByElementCondition{ // the rule's condition is specified as *ByElementCondition*, targeting a specific element symbol 
refitem:>>dependencyOwner{ 
dependencyfromModel::CustomStyleSheet::customRule::conditiontovehicle; // the condition targets the *vehicle* element 
} 
} 
}// *ByElementMetaclassCondition* examplepartpartRule:>rule{ 
part:>>condition:ByElementMetaclassCondition{// the rule's condition is specified as *ByElementMetaclassCondition*, targeting symbols by element metaclass 
refitem:>>elementMetaclass= SysML::Systems::PartUsage.metadata; // the condition targets elements with the *PartUsage* metaclasses 
} 
}// *ByMetadataAnnotationCondition*examplepart metadataApprovalRule :> rule {part :>> condition : ByMetadataAnnotationCondition {// the rule's condition is specified as *ByMetadataAnnotationCondition*, targeting symbols by element metadata 
 ref item :>> annotatingMetadataType = 'Vehicle Metadata Definitions'::Approval.metadata;// the condition targets elements with the applied *Approval* metadata 
 }}// *ByDiagramTypeCondition*examplepart generalViewRule :> rule {part :>> condition : ByDiagramTypeCondition {// the rule's condition is specified as *ByDiagramTypeCondition*, targeting symbols by view definition 
ref item :>> diagramType = DS_Views::SymbolicViews::gv.metadata; // the condition targets views defined by the *General View*view definition 
 }}// *FreeFormCondition*examplepartMyFreeformRule:>rule{ 
part:>>condition:FreeFormCondition{ // the rule's condition is specified as *FreeFormCondition*, targeting symbols by the specified expression 
calc:>>test{ 
'VCCU View'.metadata==diagram// targets element symbols on the specific view '*VCCU View*' 
 // ORelement== VCCU.metadata// targets the *VCCU* element symbol on all views (to which the style sheet is applied)} 
} 
}

###### Specifying conditions for a rule via the Specification panel

To specify a condition for a rule via the Specification panel

1. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification panel' space='UAF2P'] for the style sheet's rule part usage element.
2. Specify the condition in the Specification panel's condition compartment:
  1. Specify the needed condition in the Match by field. Click the field to view the dropdown menu with available conditions, then click the needed condition to specify it for the rule.
  2. Specify the condition values in the value field. The value field name depends on the specified condition: ConditionValue Field NameDescriptionSpecific ElementsElementDrag and drop an element from the Containment tree or a view to specify the value.What happens in the Textual Editor: The feature value of the condition's item redefines *dependencyOwner*.Element KindMetaclassDrag and drop a metaclass (e.g. metaclass from KerML library or metadata definition from SysML library) from the Containment tree or a view to specify the value.What happens in the Textual Editor: The feature value of the condition's item redefines *elementMetaclass.*Metadata AnnotationMetadata DefinitionDrag and drop a metadata definition from the Containment tree or a view to specify the value.What happens in the Textual Editor: The feature value of the condition's item redefines *annotatingMetadataType.*View TypeView DefinitionDrag and drop a view definition from the Containment tree or a view to specify the value.What happens in the Textual Editor: The feature value of the condition's item redefines *diagramType*.Custom ExpressionExpressionSpecify the expression in the Textual Editor. [ATTACHMENT filename='condition specification.png']

##### Specifying styles for a rule

There are two ways you can specify a style for a rule:

- Local specification allows you to specify the style of a specific rule only.
  - See the procedures:
    - [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] .
    - [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P']
- External specification allows you to create a custom style definition outside the rule itself, which can then be reused for style specification of different rules.
  - See the procedure [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] .

###### Specifying style attributes locally for the style of a rule via the Textual Editor

To specify style attributes locally for the style of a rule via the Textual Editor

1. Within the body of the part element of the rule, after the condition specification, declare a view usage, define it by the needed style definition, and redefine the style element inherited from the StyleSheet element.
2. Within the body of the view element, d eclare an attribute usage, redefine the needed attribute and specify its value. The available attributes depend on the style definitions (primary or custom)used for the view's definition:For a list of primary style definitions, their attributes, and value types, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P']page.To create custom style definitions, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] procedure.To define by multiple style definitions, list them in a comma-separated list.
3. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications' space='UAF2P'].

part partRule :> rule {part:>>condition:ByElementMetaclassCondition{ 
refitem:>>elementMetaclass= SysML::Systems::PartUsage.metadata; 
} 
view:ShapeStyle:>>style{ // the rule's style is defined by a primary style definition *StyleShape* 
attribute:>>textColordefault"#FF0F37";// local modification of an available attribute's value 
} 
}

###### Specifying style attributes locally for the style of a rule via the Specification panel

To specify style attributes locally for the style of a rule via the Specification panel

1. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification panel' space='UAF2P'] for the style sheet's rule part usage element.
2. In the Specification panel's style attributes compartment:
  1. Specify the style definition in the Type field:
    1. Click the input field to view the dropdown menu with available style definitions. Click the needed one to specify it as the type. [ATTACHMENT filename='style definitions dropdown menu.png']
    2. To remove the specified style definition, click the [ATTACHMENT filename='delete specified style definition button.png'] button next to the style definition. [ATTACHMENT filename='delete specified style definition.png']
    3. To remove all specified style definitions, click the [ATTACHMENT filename='More button for style definition.png'] button in the Type input field, then click Clear All . [ATTACHMENT filename='clear all types.png']
  2. Specify the style attributes:
    1. Modify the owned attributes in the Owned section:
      1. See the procedure [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification panel' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification panel' space='UAF2P'] page.
    2. Redefine inherited attributes in the Inherited section and then modify them as needed:
      1. See the procedure [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification panel' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification panel' space='UAF2P'] page.
      2. Then see the procedure [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification panel' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification panel' space='UAF2P'] page.

###### Hiding style attributes from the Symbol Style dialog for specific element kinds

To hide style attributes from the Symbol Style dialog for specific element kinds

1. Within the body of the part element of the rule, after the condition specification, declare a view usage, define it by the needed style definition, and redefine the style element inherited from the StyleSheet element.
2. Within the body of the view element, d eclare an attribute usage and apply the InvisibleInDialog metadata to it, then redefine the style attribute you want to hide from the Symbol Style dialog for the element kind specified in the rule's condition . The available attributes depend on the style definitions (primary or custom)used for the view's definition.For a list of primary style definitions and their attributes, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P']page.For more information on the Symbol Style dialog, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Modifying styles of individual symbols' space='UAF2P'] page.
3. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications' space='UAF2P'].

part partRule :> rule {part:>>condition:ByElementMetaclassCondition{ 
refitem:>>elementMetaclass= SysML::Systems::PartUsage.metadata; 
} 
view:ShapeStyle:>>style{ 
#InvisibleInDialogattribute:>>contentFillColor; // the style attribute *Content Fill Color* is hidden from the Symbol Style dialog for part usages} 
}

###### Creating custom style definitions

Unlike local attribute specification, creating custom style definitions allows you to reuse them for style specification of multiple rules.

You can create custom style definitions specifying the needed attributes and their values. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Custom style sheets' space='UAF2P'] must subclassify [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Custom style sheets' space='UAF2P'] (such as *ShapeStyle, ShapeOnBorderStyle*, etc.), inheriting their attributes, which you can modify. However, you can only add attributes that are available to the primary style definition that the custom style definition subclassifies. 
For an extensive list of primary style definitions and their available attributes, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] on the[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] page.

To create a custom style definition

1. Within the body of the part definition of the new style sheet, d eclare a view definition element, specify its name, and subclassify a primary style definition from the DS_Styles::CoreStylesComponents::KerMLStyles package. For a list of primary style definitions, their attributes, and value types, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P']page.
2. Within the body of the view definition element, d eclare an attribute usage, r edefine the needed attribute and specify the attribute's value. The available attributes and their value types depend on the primary style definition you are using.For an extensive list of the primary style definitions and their available attributes, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P']page.
3. Specify the custom style definition for the style of a rule.
4. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications' space='UAF2P'].

partdefNewStyleSheet:>StyleSheet{ 
partpartRule:>rule{ 
part:>>condition:ByElementMetaclassCondition{ // custom rule 
ref item :>> elementMetaclass = SysML::Systems::PartUsage.metadata; 
} 
view : PartTextStyleRule :>> style; // the style of the rule is updated to be defined by the new custom style definition 
} 
viewdefPartTextStyleRule:>ShapeStyle{ // new custom style definition subclassifies the primary style definition *ShapeStyle* 
attribute :>> textColor default "#68FF70"; 
} 
}

###### Creating custom reusable style attribute values

You can create custom style attributes whose values you can reuse by referencing them where needed. Additionally, you can create custom style classes grouping such attributes.

To create custom reusable style attribute values

1. Declare an attribute, s pecify its name, then define it by the needed value type, and s pecify its value.
2. (Optional) To group attributes within a custom style class, declare a part usage, specify its name, then place the attributes within the part's body.
3. Reuse the newly created style attribute values for [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] or [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] . Use [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Managing textual notation' space='UAF2P'] for attributes nested within [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'].
4. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications' space='UAF2P'].

partdefNewStyleSheet:>StyleSheet{ 
partpartRule:>rule{ 
part:>>condition:ByElementMetaclassCondition{ 
refitem:>>elementMetaclass= SysML::Systems::PartUsage.metadata; 
} 
view:PartTextStyleRule:>>style; // the custom style is passed to the rule's style 
} 
viewdefPartTextStyleRule:>ShapeStyle{ 
attribute:>>penColordefaultcustomColorPalette.customDarkGreen; // the custom color from a custom style class is reused in a custom style definition 
} 
partcustomColorPalette{// custom style class with reusable style attributes for custom color values are specified 
attributecustomDarkGreen:Colordefault"#357F35"; 
attributecustomLightGreen:Colordefault"#BFF7AA"; 
} 
}

##### Specifying the compartment style of a rule

To specify the compartment style of a rule

1. Within the body of the view element, declare a part usage, specify its name (optional), then d efine it by the appropriate compartment style definition. To determine which primary compartment style definitions are available for each element symbol, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] page.
2. Within the body, redefine the needed compartment style attribute followed by the appropriate attribute value. **** To determine which attributes and what value types are available to each primary compartment style definition, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] page.
3. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications' space='UAF2P']. partpartRule:>rule{ 
part:>>condition:ByElementMetaclassCondition{ 
refitem:>>elementMetaclass= SysML::Systems::PartUsage.metadata; 
} 
view:ShapeStyle:>>style{ // defined bya primary style definition 
attributeCompartment :AttributesCompartmentStyle{ // attribute for the attributes compartment's 
:>>showCompartmentdefaulttrue; // modifying the *showCompartment* value 
} 
} 
}
