with the <em>ByElementCondition </em>condition and <em>ShapeStyle </em>style, which includes redefinitions for <em>fillColor </em>(with a randomly assigned color value)<em> </em>and <em>penColor </em>(with a comparatively darker color value) attributes. You can modify them as needed, see <ac:link ac:anchor="Specifying conditions for a rule"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Creating style sheet components" /></ac:link> and <ac:link ac:anchor="Specifying styles for a rule"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Creating style sheet components" /></ac:link><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">.<br /><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="create rule.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Creating style sheet components" /></ri:attachment></ac:image><br /></span></li></ol><ac:structured-macro ac:name="panel" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="8cbf90ff-e87a-42e3-b4b0-de3192421c94"><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">part</span><span style="color:var(--ds-chart-gray-bold,#8590a2);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">part1</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> :&gt; </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">rule</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> {</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">   </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">part</span><span style="color:var(--ds-chart-gray-bold,#8590a2);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> :&gt;&gt; </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">condition</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> : </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-teal,#206a83);">DS_Styles::CoreStylesComponents::Predicates::ByElementCondition</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);">;</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);">   </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">part</span><span style="color:var(--ds-chart-gray-bold,#8590a2);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> :&gt;&gt; </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">style</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> : </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-teal,#206a83);">DS_Styles::CoreStylesComponents::KerMLStyles::ShapeStyle</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> {</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">      </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">attribute</span><span style="color:var(--ds-chart-gray-bold,#8590a2);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> :&gt;&gt; </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">fillColor</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> = </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-red,#ae2e24);">&quot;#81c784&quot;</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);">;</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);">      </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">attribute</span><span style="color:var(--ds-chart-gray-bold,#8590a2);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> :&gt;&gt; </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">penColor</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> = </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-red,#ae2e24);">&quot;#3e6140&quot;</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);">;</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);">   }</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);">}</span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><h4>Creating custom rules via the Specification panel</h4><p>To create a custom rule via the Specification panel</p><hr /><ol><li data-uuid="cc9a42e4-dde5-43b5-ae82-ede9fd8eda1e"><ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Creating style sheets" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Create a style sheet]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link>.</li><li data-uuid="185be77e-4987-4f6c-8d3b-48395534aea8">Create the <em>rule</em> part usage element for the style sheet's part definition element via the Specification panel by following the <ac:link ac:anchor="Creating an element via the Specification panel"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Specification panel" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Creating an element via the Specification panel]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> procedure.<br />A rule is created with the <em>ByElementCondition (Specific Elements) </em>condition and <em>ShapeStyle </em>style, which includes redefinitions for <em>fillColor </em>(with a randomly assigned color value)<em> </em>and <em>penColor </em>(with a comparatively darker color value) attributes. You can modify them as needed, see <ac:link ac:anchor="Specifying conditions for a rule"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Creating style sheet components" /></ac:link> and <ac:link ac:anchor="Specifying styles for a rule"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Creating style sheet components" /></ac:link><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">.<br /><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="Creating custom rules via the Specification panel.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Creating style sheet components" /></ri:attachment></ac:image><br /></span></li></ol><ac:structured-macro ac:name="panel" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="d9f6b832-784b-429d-b202-f1dd0f9850ed"><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">part</span><span style="color:var(--ds-chart-gray-bold,#8590a2);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">part1</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> :&gt; </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">rule</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> {</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">   </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">part</span><span style="color:var(--ds-chart-gray-bold,#8590a2);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> :&gt;&gt; </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">condition</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> : </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-teal,#206a83);">DS_Styles::CoreStylesComponents::Predicates::ByElementCondition</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);">;</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);">   </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">part</span><span style="color:var(--ds-chart-gray-bold,#8590a2);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> :&gt;&gt; </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">style</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> : </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-teal,#206a83);">DS_Styles::CoreStylesComponents::KerMLStyles::ShapeStyle</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> {</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">      </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">attribute</span><span style="color:var(--ds-chart-gray-bold,#8590a2);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> :&gt;&gt; </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">fillColor</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> = </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-red,#ae2e24);">&quot;#81c784&quot;</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);">;</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);">      </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">attribute</span><span style="color:var(--ds-chart-gray-bold,#8590a2);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> :&gt;&gt; </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">penColor</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> = </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-red,#ae2e24);">&quot;#3e6140&quot;</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);">;</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);">   }</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);">}</span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><h3>Specifying conditions for a rule</h3><p>You can specify the condition for a rule via the Textual Editor or the Specification panel. The names of the conditions differ based on the chosen specification method. See the comparison table below.</p><table class="wrapped"><colgroup><col /><col /></colgroup><tbody><tr><th>Condition Element Name in Textual Editor</th><th>Condition Name in Specification Panel</th></tr><tr><td>ByElementCondition</td><td>Specific Elements</td></tr><tr><td>ByElementMetaclassCondition</td><td>Element Kind</td></tr><tr><td>ByMetadataAnnotationCondition</td><td>Metadata Annotation</td></tr><tr><td>ByDiagramTypeCondition</td><td>View Type</td></tr><tr><td>FreeFormCondition</td><td>Custom Expression</td></tr></tbody></table><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">For more information, see the <span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"><span><ac:link ac:anchor="Style sheet rule conditions table"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Style sheet rule conditions table]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span> on the <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables" /></ac:link><span> </span>page.</span></span></p><h4>Specifying conditions for a rule via the Textual Editor</h4><p>To specify a condition for a rule via the Textual Editor</p><hr /><ol><li><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">Within the body of the part element of the rule, declare a part usage and r</span>edefine the <em>condition </em>element inherited from the <em>StyleSheet</em> element, then define it by the needed condition.</li><li>Within the body of the condition, declare a <em>ref item</em>, then r<span>edefine the needed item </span><span>and specify its values.</span><ol><li data-uuid="eac01675-9514-4d75-bf05-2cb28b9f2b89">For the <em>ByElementCondition</em>, in its body, declare a <em>ref item</em> and redefine <em>dependencyOwner</em>. In its body, declare a <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Dependency" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[dependency]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> from the rule's condition to the target element.</li><li data-uuid="324224b0-6b91-4f31-8bff-0fc1177b7e1d">For the <em>FreeFormCondition</em>, declare a <em>calc </em>and redefine <em>test</em>, then specify the needed expression.<br /><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="66f6e464-a7c3-442a-a23a-47fbe9442747"><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">The available ref items and their value types depend on the condition definition you are using. For a list of the condition definitions and their available ref items, see the <span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"><span><ac:link ac:anchor="Style sheet rule conditions table"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Style sheet rule conditions table]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span> on the <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables" /></ac:link><span> </span>page.</span></span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li></ol></li><li><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);"><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);"><ac:link ac:anchor="Synchronizing modifications"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Synchronize modifications]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span>.<br /></span><ac:structured-macro ac:name="panel" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="54ec3c1e-f836-4456-9c0a-556a564fff5c"><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);"> <span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-green-bolder,#164b35);">// <em>ByElementCondition</em> example</span></span></p><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">part</span><span style="color:var(--ds-chart-gray-bold,#8590a2);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">customRule</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> :&gt; </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">rule</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> {</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">   </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">part</span><span style="color:var(--ds-chart-gray-bold,#8590a2);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#000000);"> :&gt;&gt; </span><span  </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">dependency</span><span style="color:var(--ds-chart-gray-bold,#8590a2);"> </span><span /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">      </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">calc</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">:&gt;&gt; </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">test</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> {</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">         '</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">VCCU View'</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">.</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">metadata</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> == </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">diagram</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-green-bolder,#164b35);">// targets element symbols on the specific view '<em>VCCU View</em>'<br />         // OR<br /></span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">         element</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> == VCCU.</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">metadata</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-green-bolder,#164b35);">// targets the <em>VCCU</em> element symbol on all views (to which the style sheet is applied)</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">      <br />      }</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">   }</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">}</span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li></ol><h4>Specifying conditions for a rule via the Specification panel</h4><p>To specify a condition for a rule via the Specification panel</p><hr /><ol><li data-uuid="00415ffd-14b2-4106-9237-d0dc14b8479a"><ac:link ac:anchor="Opening the Specification panel"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Specification panel" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Open the Specification panel]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> for the style sheet's <em>rule</em> part usage element.</li><li data-uuid="7588cd53-1a65-491b-b39d-309f586f9e44">Specify the condition in the Specification panel's <strong>condition </strong>compartment:<ol><li data-uuid="fec36ec4-733e-46d3-9f1b-d2910bee539c">Specify the needed condition in the <strong>Match by</strong> field. Click the field to view the dropdown menu with available conditions, then click the needed condition to specify it for the rule.</li><li data-uuid="035ff853-26f3-4643-a1a1-028e43db250b">Specify the condition values in the value field. The value field name depends on the specified condition:<br /><table class="wrapped" style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;"><colgroup class=""><col class="" /><col class="" /><col class="" /></colgroup><tbody class=""><tr class=""><th>Condition</th><th>Value Field Name</th><th>Description</th></tr><tr class=""><td>Specific Elements</td><td>Element</td><td><p>Drag and drop an element from the Containment tree or a view to specify the value.</p><p>What happens in the Textual Editor: The feature value of the condition's item redefines <em>dependencyOwner</em>.</p></td></tr><tr class=""><td>Element Kind</td><td>Metaclass</td><td><p>Drag and drop a metaclass (e.g. metaclass from KerML library or metadata definition from SysML library) from the Containment tree or a view to specify the value.</p><p>What happens in the Textual Editor: The feature value of the condition's item redefines <em>elementMetaclass.</em></p></td></tr><tr class=""><td>Metadata Annotation</td><td>Metadata Definition</td><td><p>Drag and drop a metadata definition from the Containment tree or a view to specify the value.</p><p>What happens in the Textual Editor: The feature value of the condition's item redefines <em>annotatingMetadataType.</em></p></td></tr><tr class=""><td>View Type</td><td>View Definition</td><td><p>Drag and drop a view definition from the Containment tree or a view to specify the value.</p><p>What happens in the Textual Editor: The feature value of the condition's item redefines <em>diagramType</em>.</p></td></tr><tr class=""><td>Custom Expression</td><td>Expression</td><td>Specify the expression in the Textual Editor.</td></tr></tbody></table><br /><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="condition specification.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Creating style sheet components" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></li></ol></li></ol><h3>Specifying styles for a rule</h3><p>There are two ways you can specify a style for a rule:</p><ul><li>Local specification allows you to specify the style of a specific rule only.<ul><li data-uuid="2000a681-ca91-4dbb-b733-bbdd3631ae5e">See the procedures: <ul><li definition outside the rule itself, which can then be reused for style specification of different rules.<ul><li data-uuid="9e725475-3662-4b9f-af5f-e2244d79587b">See the procedure <ac:link page.</li></ol></li></ol></li></ol></li></ol><h4>Hiding style attributes from the Symbol Style dialog for specific element kinds</h4><p>To hide style attributes from the Symbol Style dialog for condition specification, </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">declare a view usage, define it by the needed style definition, and </span>redefine the <em>style </em>element inherited an attribute usage and apply the <em>InvisibleInDialog </em>metadata to it, then redefine the style attribute you want to hide from the Symbol Style dialog for the element kind specified in the rule's condition<span>.<br /></span><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="922934b4-4737-4b7b-a1b2-9b180f221f01"><ac:rich-text-body><ul><li><span>The available attributes depend on the style definitions <span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">(primary or custom) </span>used for the view's definition. </span>For a list of primary style definitions and their attributes, see the <span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"><span><ac:link ac:anchor="Symbol styles table"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Symbol styles table]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span> on the</span> <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables" /></ac:link><span> </span>page.</li><li data-uuid="14d743eb-5b86-41e9-86f0-1a15c1a8cbec">For more information on the Symbol Style dialog, see the <ac:link><ri:page data-uuid="4d20e455-c815-4318-87bc-6fe4f415e4f9"><span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);"><ac:link ac:anchor="Synchronizing modifications"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Synchronize modifications]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span>.</span></li></ol><ac:structured-macro ac:name="panel" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="18071fed-1f01-4d4f-98fd-7271fa24e1ba"><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">part <span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);"><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">partRule</span> :&gt; <span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">rule</span> {</span><br /></span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">   part</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">:&gt;&gt; </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">condition</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> : </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> = SysML::Systems::PartUsage.</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">metadata</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">;</span><br style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> :&gt;&gt; </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">style</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> { </span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">     </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">#</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-teal,#206a83);">InvisibleInDialog</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">attribute</span><span style="color:var(--ds-chart-gray-bold,#8590a2);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> <span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-green-bolder,#164b35);">// the style attribute <em>Content Fill Color</em> is hidden from the Symbol Style dialog for part usages<br /></span></span></span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">   }</span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">}</span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><h4>Creating custom style definitions</h4><p>Unlike local attribute specification, creating custom style definitions allows you to reuse them for style specification of multiple rules. </p><p>You can create custom style definitions specifying the needed attributes and their values. <ac:link ac:anchor="Style sheet composition"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Custom style sheets" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Custom style definitions]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> must subclassify <ac:link ac:anchor="Style sheet composition"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Custom style sheets" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[primary style definitions]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> (such as <em>ShapeStyle, ShapeOnBorderStyle</em>, etc.), inheriting their attributes, which you can modify. However, you can only add attributes that are available to the primary style definition that the custom style definition subclassifies. <br />For an extensive list of primary style definitions and their available attributes, see the <span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"><span><ac:link ac:anchor="Symbol styles table"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Symbol styles table]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span> on the </span><ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables" /></ac:link> page.<br /><br /></p><p>To create a custom style definition</p><hr /><ol><li><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">Within the body of the part definition of the new style sheet, d</span>eclare a view definition element, specify its name, and subclassify a primary style definition<span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;"> from the </span><em>DS_Styles::CoreStylesComponents::KerMLStyles </em><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">package. </span><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="596add9c-8bf9-4461-ba72-634bce333c7d"><ac:rich-text-body><p>For a list of primary style definitions, their attributes, and value types, see the <span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"><span><ac:link ac:anchor="Symbol styles table"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Symbol styles table]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link></span> on the</span> <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables" /></ac:link><span> </span>page.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li><li><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">Within the body of the view definition element, <!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=298090601 space=UAF2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 00208: COPY Creating style sheets

- page_id: `298090601`
- space_key: `UAF2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UAF2P/pages/298090601/COPY+Creating+style+sheets
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-03-26T12:07:24.586+01:00`
- ancestors: COPY Symbol styles > COPY Custom style sheets
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

You can create custom rule-based symbol styles by creating a style sheet. However, there are two ways you can do that:

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] This option allows you to create your own custom rules as well as reuse and customize all the rules already available in the reused style sheet. The reused style sheet can be either a predefined one (e.g., *DefaultStyleSheet*) or a custom-created one. For example, you can reuse the *DefaultStyleSheet*style sheet, then customize its rules by changing their names, attributes, and their values, etc. Additionally, if you create rules only for selected symbols, overwriting the DefaultStyle*Sheet* 's rules, all the other symbols you do not overwrite will continue to be represented according to the DefaultStyle*Sheet* .
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] This option allows you to create your own custom rules only without reusing any predefined or custom style sheets and their rules . Choose this option if you prefer creating your own rules without the need to reuse or customize the existing ones.

##### Creating a style sheet

###### Reusing an existing style sheet

To reuse an existing style sheet

1. In the Containment tree, [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Managing elements' space='UAF2P'] .
2. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Managing Textual Editor' space='UAF2P'] for the new namespace.
3. In the Textual Editor, [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Package' space='UAF2P'] and name it.
4. Within the body of the package, [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Importing and filtering elements' space='UAF2P'] the DS_Styles , CoreStylesComponents, Predicates , ColorDefinitions , CompartmentVisibilityDefinitions , KerMLStyles , and SysMLStyles packages. To learn more about each package, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Custom style sheets' space='UAF2P'] section on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Custom style sheets' space='UAF2P'] page.
5. Declare a part definition, specify the name for the new style sheet, subclassify the part definition of the existing style sheet you want to reuse (e.g., DefaultStyleSheet ). You can now [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] or [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Customizing style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] within the body of the new part definition.

packageNewStylesPackage{privateimportDS_Styles::**;privateimportCoreStylesComponents::*; 
privateimportPredicates::*; 
privateimportColorDefinitions::*; 
privateimportCompartmentVisibilityDefinitions::*; 
privateimportKerMLStyles::*; 
privateimportSysMLStyles::*; 
partdefNewStyleSheet:>DefaultStyleSheet{ 
// specify custom rules or customize those in the *DefaultStyleSheet* style sheet here 
} 
}

###### Creating a custom style sheet from scratch

To create a custom style sheet from scratch

1. In the Containment tree, [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Managing elements' space='UAF2P'] .
2. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Managing Textual Editor' space='UAF2P'] for the new namespace.
3. In the Textual Editor, [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Package' space='UAF2P'] and name it.
4. Within the body of the package, [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Importing and filtering elements' space='UAF2P'] the DS_Styles , CoreStylesComponents, Predicates , ColorDefinitions , CompartmentVisibilityDefinitions , KerMLStyles , and SysMLStyles packages. To learn more about each package, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Custom style sheets' space='UAF2P'] section on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Custom style sheets' space='UAF2P'] page.
5. Declare a part definition with the part def keyword, specify the name for the new style sheet, subclassify the StyleSheet part definition. You can now [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] within the body of the new part definition.

package NewStylesPackage {privateimportDS_Styles::**;privateimportCoreStylesComponents::*; 
privateimportPredicates::*; 
privateimportColorDefinitions::*; 
privateimportCompartmentVisibilityDefinitions::*; 
privateimportKerMLStyles::*; 
privateimportSysMLStyles::*;part def NewStyleSheet :>StyleSheet{ 
 // specify custom rules here } 
}

###### Creating a custom style sheet from scratch via the Style Sheets button and activating it for a specific view

To create a custom style sheet from scratch via the Style Sheets button and activate it for a specific view

1. Open a specific view.
2. Click the Style Sheets button in the view toolbar . In the dropdown menu, click the **Create and** Apply Style Sheet command. A part definition element for the new style sheet is created, and its element symbol is displayed in the view. The style sheet is also automatically activated for this view. 
You can now [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] within the body of the new part definition. The created style sheet is empty; it does not contain any imports necessary for the style sheet component creation. For that, either see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] procedure or use qualified names to access the needed elements.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=298090596 space=UAF2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 00209: COPY Custom style sheets

- page_id: `298090596`
- space_key: `UAF2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UAF2P/pages/298090596/COPY+Custom+style+sheets
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-03-26T12:07:24.349+01:00`
- ancestors: COPY Symbol styles
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

Instead of or in addition to using the default style sheet that specifies the default symbol styles, you can create your own custom model-based symbol styles by creating style sheets with your own sets of rules.

##### Working with style sheets

Custom model-based symbol styles are specified in a style sheet. There can be several types of style sheets:

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Predefined style sheets' space='UAF2P'] . The predefined style sheets are located in the *DS_Styles::StyleSheets*package of the*3DS**SysML Customization*library. There are two predefined style sheets in the*DS_Styles::StyleSheets*package:
  - DefaultStyleSheet
  - BlackAndWhiteStyleSheet
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] . There are two types of style sheets you can create:
  - [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] This option allows you to create your own custom rules as well as reuse and customize all the rules already available in the reused style sheet. The reused style sheet can be either a predefined one (e.g., *DefaultStyleSheet*) or a custom-created one. For example, you can reuse the *DefaultStyleSheet*style sheet, then customize its rules by changing their names, attributes, and their values, etc. Additionally, if you create rules only for selected symbols, overwriting the DefaultStyle*Sheet* 's rules, all the other symbols you do not overwrite will continue to be represented according to the DefaultStyle*Sheet* .
  - [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] This option allows you to create your own custom rules only without reusing any predefined or custom style sheets and their rules . Choose this option if you prefer creating your own rules without the need to reuse or customize the existing ones.

##### Style sheet composition

A style sheet is comprised of the following components:

- Rules - specify conditions and styles for symbols.
  - Condition - specifies to which symbols the rule applies.
  - Style - specifies the style that will be applied to the symbols that comply with the specified condition.

#### PANEL: Example of a rule

Example of a rule

partattributeRule :> rule { 
part:>> condition : ByElementMetaclassCondition { // the 'condition' component specifying a predefined condition *ByElementMetaclassCondition* that the rule applies to symbols 
refitem:>> elementMetaclass = (SysML::Systems::AttributeUsage.metadata, SysML::Systems::AttributeDefinition.metadata); // specifying the condition with applicable element metaclasses 
} 
view:>> style : AbstractDeepPurpleStyle; // the 'style' component specifying a predefined style *AbstractDeepPurpleStyle* found in the *DS_Styles::StyleSheets::ColorDefinitions*package 
}

- Style definitions . There are several types of style definitions :
  - **Primary style definitions** - high-level style definitions that specify style attributes that can be used for a rule. They are contained in the *DS_Styles::CoreStylesComponents::KerMLStyles* of the *3DS SysML Customization*library.
    - Primary style definitions cannot be edited and should be used to [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] or [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'].
    - For a list of primary style definitions, see the 'Primary style definitions' column in the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'].
  - **Auxiliary style definitions** - lower-level style definitions that reuse (subclassify) primary style definitions, specifying selected attributes and their values of the primary style definition. Auxiliary style definitions allow you to specify concrete styles which can then be reused in multiple rules instead of specifying the style for each rule locally. There are two types of auxiliary style definitions:
    - Predefined style definitions - style definitions specified in the DS_Styles::StyleSheets::ColorDefinitions package of the *3DS SysML Customization*library (e.g., AbstractGreenStyle , AbstractRedStyle , etc.).
      - Predefined style definitions cannot be edited, but they can be customized locally to [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Customizing style sheet components' space='UAF2P'].
      - For a list of predefined style definitions, see the 'Predefined style definitions' column in the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'].
    - **Custom style definitions** - style definitions you create yourself.

#### PANEL: Explanation in textual notation

Explanation in textual notation

// primary style definitions *SymbolStyle*and *ShapeStyle*in the *DS_Styles::CoreStylesComponents::KerMLStyles*package

viewdefSymbolStyle { 
attributelineWidth : Integerdefault1; 
attributefillColor : Colordefault"#FFF0F0F0"; 
attributeuseFillColor : Booleandefaulttrue; 
attributepenColor : Colordefault"#FF424242"; 
attributetextColor : Colordefault"#000000"; 
attributefont : Fontdefault"Roboto,0,11"; 
attributewrap : Booleandefaultfalse; 
}

viewdefShapeStyle:>SymbolStyle{ 
attributecontentFillColor:Colordefault"#FFFFFFFF"{ 
} 
attributetextVerticalPosition:TextVerticalPositionEnumdefaulttextVerticalPosition::Top{ 
} 
attributecompartmentFillColor:Colordefault"#FFF0F0F0"; 
attributecompartmentTextColor:Colordefault"#000000"; 
}

// predefined (auxiliary) style definition *AbstractDeepPurpleStyle*specified for the *attributeRule* rule (external specification) in the *DS_Styles::StyleSheets::ColorDefinitions*package

part attributeRule :> rule { 
 part:>> condition : ByElementMetaclassCondition { 
 ref item :>> elementMetaclass = (SysML::Systems::AttributeUsage.metadata, SysML::Systems::AttributeDefinition.metadata); 
 } 
 view:>> style : AbstractDeepPurpleStyle; // the predefined style definition *AbstractDeepPurpleStyle***is specified for the style component of the *attributeRule* rule (external specification) 
}

viewdefAbstractDeepPurpleStyle:>ShapeStyle{ // predefined (auxiliary) style definition *AbstractDeepPurpleStyle*in the *DS_Styles::StyleSheets::ColorDefinitions*packagethat subclassifies *ShapeStyle* 
attribute:>>fillColordefault"#E6DEF3"; 
attribute:>>compartmentFillColordefault"#F8F5FB"; 
attribute:>>penColordefault"#20125F"; 
}

##### 3DS SysML Customization library structure

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

The [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Libraries & samples' space='UAF2P']*3DS SysML Customization*library contains the *DassaultSystemesStyles*namespace, dedicated to symbol styles' customization:

- <DS_Styles> DassaultSystemesStyles
  - CoreStylesComponents
    - Contains style sheet modeling and configuration concepts.
    - **KerMLStyles**. Contains primary style definitions that can be reused (subclassified) for style sheet rules . For a list of the primary style definitions, their ref items, and their compatibility with element symbols, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] page.
    - **SysMLStyles**. Contains compartment style view definitions for style sheet rules.
    - **Predicates**. Contains condition part definitions for style sheet rules. To learn more about reusing and modifying existing or creating custom rules using primary style definitions, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Customizing style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] pages.
  - **StyleSheets**.
    - Contains [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Predefined style sheets' space='UAF2P']. You can reuse and customize the predefined style sheets or create new ones from scratch. See the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] page.
    - **ColorDefinitions**. Contains color definitions for style sheet rules. You can reuse and customize the predefined style definitions. See the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Customizing style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] page.For a list of predefined style definitions, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] page.
    - **CompartmentVisibilityDefinitions**. Contains compartment visibility definitions for style sheet rules .

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html
<p>Instead of or in addition to using the default style sheet that specifies the default symbol styles, you can create your own custom model-based symbol styles <span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">by creating style sheets with your own sets of rules. </span></p><h3>Working with style sheets</h3><p>Custom model-based symbol styles are specified in a style sheet. <span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">There can be several types of style sheets:</span></p><ul><li><ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Predefined style sheets" /></ac:link>. <span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">The predefined style sheets are located in the <em style="text-align: left;">DS_Styles::StyleSheets</em><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"><span> </span>package of the<span> <span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);"><em>3DS </em></span><em style="text-align: left;">SysML Customization</em></span><span> </span>library.</span></span> </span></span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">There are two predefined style sheets in the<span> <em>DS_Styles::StyleSheets</em> </span>package:</span></span><ul><li><em>DefaultStyleSheet</em></li><li><em>BlackAndWhiteStyleSheet</em></li></ul></li><li><ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Creating style sheets" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[User-created style sheets]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link>. There are two types of style sheets you can create:<ul><li><ac:link ac:anchor="Reusing an existing style sheet"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Creating style sheets" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Reuse an existing style sheet]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">This option allows you to create your own custom rules as well as reuse and customize all the rules already available in the reused </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">style sheet. The reused style sheet can be either a predefined one (e.g., <em>DefaultStyleSheet</em>) or a custom-created one. </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">For example, you can reuse the <em>DefaultStyleSheet </em>style sheet, then customize its </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">rules </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">by changing their names, attributes, and their values, etc. Additionally, if you create rules only for selected symbols, overwriting the<span> </span></span><em style="text-align: left;">DefaultStyle<em>Sheet</em></em><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">'s rules, all the other symbols you do not overwrite will continue to be represented according to the </span><em style="text-align: scratch]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link><br />This option allows you to create your own custom rules only without reusing any predefined or custom style sheets and their rules<span>. </span>Choose this option if you prefer creating your own rules without the need to reuse or customize the existing ones. </li></ul></li></ul><h3>Style sheet composition</h3><p>A style symbols the rule applies.</li><li><strong>Style </strong>- specifies the style that will be applied to the symbols that comply with the specified condition. </li></ul></li></ul><ac:structured-macro <!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=298090604 space=UAF2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 00210: COPY Customizing style sheet components

- page_id: `298090604`
- space_key: `UAF2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UAF2P/pages/298090604/COPY+Customizing+style+sheet+components
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-03-26T12:07:24.816+01:00`
- ancestors: COPY Symbol styles > COPY Custom style sheets
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

See the procedures on this page for customizing the style sheet components.

- The procedures on this page use the example of customizing rules of the DefaultStyleSheet style sheet, however, customization of any other style sheet's rules, whether predefined or custom, is analogous.
- For procedures on supplementing customized style sheets with your own custom rules (instead of or in addition to customizing existing ones), see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] page.

##### Customizing style sheet components

###### Reusing style sheet**rules

To reuse style sheet rules

1. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheets' space='UAF2P']Reuse a**style sheet (e.g., DefaultStyleSheet ).
2. Within the body of the part definition of the new style sheet, declare a part usage, specify a new name for the rule (optional), redefine the needed rule, and in its body, do any of the following as needed:
  1. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Customizing style sheet components' space='UAF2P'].
  2. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Customizing style sheet components' space='UAF2P'].
  3. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Customizing style sheet components' space='UAF2P'].
3. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications' space='UAF2P']. partPortRule rule defined in the DefaultStyleSheet style sheetpackageNewStylesPackage{privateimportDS_Styles::**;privateimportCoreStylesComponents::*; 
 privateimportPredicates::*; 
 privateimportColorDefinitions::*; 
 privateimportCompartmentVisibilityDefinitions::*; 
 privateimportKerMLStyles::*; 
 privateimportSysMLStyles::*; 
partdefNewStyleSheet:>DefaultStyleSheet{partcustomizedPartPortRule:>>partPortRule{ // redefining and renaming the *partPortRule* rule 
// customize the redefined rule 
} 
} 
}

###### Modifying the style definition defining the style of a rule

To modify the style definition defining the style of a rule

1. Reuse a style sheet**rule[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Customizing style sheet components' space='UAF2P'].
2. Declare a view usage, define it by the needed auxiliary style definition, and redefine the inherited part *style*. You can define the view by multiple style definitions, listing them in a comma-separated list.
3. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications' space='UAF2P']. partdefNewStyleSheet:>DefaultStyleSheet{ 
partcustomizedPartPortRule:>>partPortRule{ 
view:AbstractCyanStyle:>>style; // the *AbstractGreenRule*inherited from the *partPortRule*via the *DefaultStyleSheet*style sheet is replaced with the predefined style definition *AbstractCyanStyle* 
} 
}

###### Modifying the styleattributes locallyfor the style of a rule

There are two ways you can specify a style for a rule:

- Local specification allows you to specify the style of a specific rule only. See the procedure [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Customizing style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] .
- External specification allows you to create a custom style definition outside the rule itself, which can then be reused for the style specification of different rules. See the subsection [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] page.

To modify the style attributes locally for the style of a rule

1. Reuse a style sheet**rule[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Customizing style sheet components' space='UAF2P'].
2. Declare a view usage, redefine the inherited part *style*, and in its body, redefine the needed attribute, specifying the new value. The attributes available to the specified style definition depend on the style definitions they subclassify. For an extensive list of the predefined style definitions and the primary style definitions they subclassify, and their available attributes, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] page.
3. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications' space='UAF2P']. part def NewStyleSheet:>DefaultStyleSheet{ 
partcustomizedPartPortRule:>>partPortRule{ 
view:>>style{ 
attribute :>> fillColor default "#D9EEDA"; // redefining the attribute *fillColor* available via the predefined style definition *AbstractGreenRule* 
} 
} 
}

###### Modifying thecompartment styleof a rule

The majority of the compartments are disabled (set to *false*) for most of the elements in the *DefaultStyleSheet*style sheet via the *HideAllCompartments* predefined compartment style definition.

To modify the compartment style of a rule

1. Reuse a style sheet**rule[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Customizing style sheet components' space='UAF2P'].
2. Declare a view usage, redefine the inherited part *style*. In its body, declare a part for the needed compartment and define it by its definition. In its body, redefine the needed attribute, specifying the new value. To determine which primary compartment style definitions (including their attributes and value types) are available for each element symbol, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] page.
3. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications' space='UAF2P']. partdefNewStyleSheet:>DefaultStyleSheet{ 
partnewPartPortRule:>>partPortRule{ 
view:>>style{ 
partattributeCompartment:AttributesCompartmentStyle{ 
:>>showCompartmentdefaulttrue;// the inherited *attributeCompartment* part's *showCompartment* attribute's value is changed to *true* 
} 
} 
} 
}

    </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue,#0055cc);">view</span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">: </span><span predefined style definition <em>AbstractCyanStyle</em></span></span></span><br /><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">   }</span><br /><span rule</span></h4><p>There are two ways you can specify a style for a rule:</p><ul><li>Local specification allows you to specify the style of a specific rule only. <!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=298090631 space=UAF2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 00211: COPY Modifying styles of individual symbols

- page_id: `298090631`
- space_key: `UAF2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UAF2P/pages/298090631/COPY+Modifying+styles+of+individual+symbols
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-03-26T12:07:27.610+01:00`
- ancestors: COPY Symbol styles
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

**On this page:**

You can customize the styles of individual symbols. Using the Symbol Style dialog, you can specify style properties for specific symbols, determining their appearance.

Changing the styles for an individual symbol via the Symbol Style dialog overwrites both predefined and custom model-based symbol styles; the modifications persist even after updating [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P']. To reset, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Modifying styles of individual symbols' space='UAF2P'] procedure.

##### Opening the Symbol Style dialog

To open the Symbol Style dialog

Do one of the following:

- Right-click the selected element symbol(s). In the shortcut menu, click **Symbol Style**. To invoke the Symbol Style dialog for a [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Docked symbols' space='UAF2P'], you must right-click the symbol's header.
- Select the element symbol(s) and press Alt+Enter .

##### Modifying individual symbol styles

To modify individual symbol styles

1. Select the symbol(s) whose styles you want to modify and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Modifying styles of individual symbols' space='UAF2P'] .
2. Locate the property you want to modify and change its value to the needed one in the Value column.
3. Click Close .

##### Resetting changes made in the Symbol Style dialog

While changing the styles for an individual symbol via the Symbol Style dialog overwrites both predefined and custom model-based symbol styles, you can easily undo them following the procedure below.

To reset changes made in the Symbol Style dialog

1. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Modifying styles of individual symbols' space='UAF2P'] .
2. Locate the property you want to reset to the style of the currently activated style sheet. Its check box in the Default column is deselected. [ATTACHMENT filename='Resetting_changes.png']
3. Select the check box in the Default column for the needed property.
4. Click Close .

##### The Symbol Style dialog

The table below lists the style properties available for modification and their descriptions.

- Modifying a symbol style changes its Default value to false .
- You can hide unwanted symbol styles from the Symbol Style dialog for specific element kinds. See the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] procedure on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] page.

In the **Symbol Style** dialog, symbol styles are ordered into the following groups:

- **Main**: this property group displays symbol styles available to the majority of element kinds.
- **Compartment-based properties**: the availability of specific symbol style groups depends on the element kind, as [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Compartments' space='UAF2P']. Some of the symbol styles available to individual compartment-based symbol style groups may be the same as in the Main group, while others are compartment-specific.
  - Compartment-based style groups can be: Documentation, Objective, Subject, Actors, Stakeholders, Include Use Cases, Parts, Ports, Parameters, Attributes, Ends, Satisfy Requirements , Items, Constraints, Require Constraints, Assume Constraints, Assert Constraints, Actions, Perform Actions, Exhibit States, Frames, Enumerations, and Metadata.

| Name | Value options | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Main |  |  |
| Line Width | Positive number | Specify the width of the symbol's outline. |
| Fill Color | SwatchesHSVHSLRGBCMYK | Specify the color of the symbol's header.To enable a gradient for this property, enable the view style property. |
| Use Fill Color | true/false | Specify whether to use a specific color for the symbol's header. |
| Pen Color | SwatchesHSVHSLRGBCMYK | Specify the color of the symbol's outline. |
| Text Color | SwatchesHSVHSLRGBCMYK | Specify the color of the symbol's text. |
| Font | Multiple font optionsMultiple style options (italic, bold, etc.)Multiple size options | Specify the font style of the symbol's text. |
| Wrap | true/false | Specify whether the text should wrap to fit the width of the element symbol. |
| Compartment Fill Color | SwatchesHSVHSLRGBCMYK | Specify the color of the symbol's compartments. |
| Compartment Text Color | SwatchesHSVHSLRGBCMYK | Specify the color for the text in the symbol's compartments. |
| Show Short Name | true/false | Specify whether the element's should be displayed on the element symbol. |
| Show Name | true/false | Specify whether the element's should be displayed on the element symbol. |
| Show Modifiers | true/false | Specify whether the element's (e.g., in, ref, abstract, etc.) should be displayed on the element symbol. The property does not control the individual and portion kind (timeslice, snapshot) modifiers. |
| Show Full Text | true/false | Specify whether element values should be displayed in full or abbreviated. Modifying this property affects the values displayed in both the selected symbol's name and its compartments.Modifying this property does not affect element values displayed in the metadata compartment. Values in this compartment are always displayed in full.The property is available for specific symbols based on the element kind. |
| Content Fill Color | SwatchesHSVHSLRGBCMYK | Specify the color of the symbol's body.To enable a gradient for this property, enable the view style property.The property is available for specific symbols based on the element kind. |
| Text Vertical Position | TopCenterBottom | Specify the element name position for the symbol.The property is available for specific symbols based on the element kind.The property is only effective for element symbols displayed without their compartments. |
| Show Specialization | true/false | Specify whether the textual symbols should be displayed in the element name (e.g., the textual symbol :> or the keyword specializes, in the case of subclassification). The property is available for specific symbols based on the element kind. |
| Show Qualified Name for Specialization | true/false | Specify whether the specialization's full should be displayed in the element name.Enabling the property also requires the 'Show Specialization' property to be enabled.The property is available for specific symbols based on the element kind. |
| Orientation | HorizontalVertical | Specify the orientation for the symbol.The property is available for specific symbols based on the element kind. |
| Path Style | RectilinearObliqueBezier | Specify the style of the path.The property is available for specific symbols based on the element kind. |
| Show Value | true/false | Specify whether the element's defined value should be displayed.The property is available for specific symbols based on the element kind. |
| Show Inherited Sign | true/false | Specify whether the inherited sign should be displayed on the symbol.The property is available for specific symbols based on the element kind. |
| Show Payload | true/false | Specify whether the payload name and sign should be displayed on the connector path.The property is available for specific symbols based on the element kind. |
| Text Horizontal Position | LeftCenterRight | Specify the text position for the vertical and horizontal separator symbols. |
| Line Style | SolidDashedDottedetc. | Specify the line style for the vertical and horizontal separator symbols. |
| Is Rounded | true/false | Specify whether the rectangular shape symbol's corners should be rounded. |
| Compartment-based symbol styles (in compartment-based symbol style groups, e.g., Documentation, Objective, Subject, Actors, etc.) |  |  |
| Show Compartment | true/false | Specify whether the compartment should be displayed or suppressed. |
| Show Inherited | true/false | Specify whether the inherited elements should be displayed on the symbol. |
| Show Only Owned | true/false | Specify whether only the owned elements or imported ones, too, should be displayed in the symbol compartment.The property is only available for the package symbol and applies to its Members compartment. |

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=298090635 space=UAF2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 00212: COPY Modifying styles of individual views

- page_id: `298090635`
- space_key: `UAF2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UAF2P/pages/298090635/COPY+Modifying+styles+of+individual+views
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-03-26T12:07:27.920+01:00`
- ancestors: COPY Symbol styles
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

The primary ways to customize the styles of individual views:

- Activating style sheets for a specific view.
- Managing style properties for a specific view via the View Style dialog.

Changing the styles for an individual view via the View Style dialog overwrites both predefined and custom model-based style sheets; the modifications persist even after updating [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P']. To reset, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Modifying styles of individual views' space='UAF2P'] procedure.

##### Activating style sheets for a specific view

- For more information, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] procedures on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] page.

##### Managing style properties for a specific view via the View Style dialog

###### Opening the View Style dialog

To open the View Style dialog

- Right-click the selected view. In the shortcut menu, click **View Style**.

###### Modifying an individual view's style

To modify an individual view's style

1. Select the view(s) whose styles you want to modify and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Modifying styles of individual views' space='UAF2P'] .
2. Locate the property you want to modify and change its value to the needed one in the Value column.
3. Click Close .

###### Resetting changes made in the View Style dialog

While changing the styles for an individual view via the View Style dialog overwrites both predefined and custom model-based style sheets, you can easily undo them following the procedure below.

To reset changes made in the View Style dialog

1. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Modifying styles of individual views' space='UAF2P'] .
2. Locate the property you want to reset to the style of the currently activated style sheet. Its check box in the Default column is deselected.
3. Select the check box in the Default column for the needed property.
4. Click Close .

###### The View Style dialog

The table below lists the style properties available for modification and their descriptions.

Modifying a view style property changes its **Default**value to *false*.

Currently, other view style properties displayed in the dialog besides the **Use Gradient Fill**are not functional.

| Name | Value options | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Main |  |  |
| Use Gradient Fill | true/false | Specify whether a gradient should be used for the Fill Color and Content Fill Color . |
| Show Line Jumps On | NoneHorizontal LineVertical Line | Specify whether line jumps should be used for intersecting lines (e.g., paths).None - line jumps are not used.Horizontal Line - line jumps are used only on horizontal lines (default).Vertical Line - line jumps are used only on vertical lines. |

To reset, see the <ac:link ac:anchor="Resetting changes made in the View Style dialog"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Modifying styles of individual views" /></ac:link> procedure. </p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><h3>Activating style sheets for a specific view</h3><ul><li data-uuid="938edd71-48e6-406d-b931-1ed573cc5ee1">For more information, see the <ac:link ac:anchor="Activating style sheets for a specific view"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Activating style sheets" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Activating style sheets for a specific view]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> procedures on the <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Activating style sheets" /></ac:link> page.</li></ul><h3>Managing style properties for a specific view via the View Style dialog</h3><h4>Opening the View Style dialog</h4><p>To open the View Style dialog</p><hr /><ul><li data-uuid="6f839a2b-f557-4b9b-a825-aef531068d51"><p class="auto-cursor-target">Right-click the selected view. In the shortcut menu, click <strong>View Style</strong>.</p></li></ul><h4>Modifying an individual view's style</h4><p>To modify an individual view's style</p><hr /><ol><li data-uuid="91062e4c-0440-47ed-8a32-febc95f40303">Select the view(s) whose styles you want to modify and <ac:link ac:anchor="Opening the View Style dialog"><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[open the View Style dialog]]></ac:plain-text-link-body><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Modifying styles of individual views" /></ac:link>.</li><li data-uuid="d5268c0f-3ece-4014-a7f3-28a7d3af21cc">Locate the property you want to modify and change its value to the needed one in the Value column.</li><li data-uuid="32d56453-b2f3-442d-b929-d3a20f13581b">Click <strong>Close</strong>.</li></ol><h4>Resetting changes made in the View Style dialog</h4><p>While changing the styles for an individual view via the View Style dialog overwrites both predefined and custom model-based style sheets, you can easily undo them following the procedure below.</p><p>To reset changes made in the View Style dialog</p><hr /><ol><li data-uuid="7f8ce54d-499f-4145-8c5c-98784a51c798"><ac:link ac:anchor="Opening the View Style dialog"><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Open the View Style dialog]]></ac:plain-text-link-body><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Modifying styles of individual views" /></ac:link>.</li><li data-uuid="3903f485-776d-4cd4-bf2d-6d37263b0599">Locate the property you want to reset to the style of the currently activated style sheet. Its check box in the <strong>Default </strong>column is deselected.</li><li data-uuid="bfdd7237-bda4-47c1-9300-2665a1f0b640">Select the check box in the <strong>Default </strong>column for the needed property.</li><li data-uuid="7b4b7649-5559-4404-b700-7d763d82f3fa">Click <strong>Close</strong>.</li></ol><h4>The View Style dialog</h4><p>The table below lists the style properties available for modification and their descriptions. </p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="2f005f26-68b4-4ee7-9f09-947dee503a50"><ac:rich-text-body><p>Modifying a view style property changes its <strong>Default </strong>value to <em>false</em>.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><ac:structured-macro ac:name="warning" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="c2ab1c2c-2c25-43f4-a19e-041fe1bab07e"><ac:rich-text-body><p>Currently, other view style properties displayed in the dialog besides the <strong>Use Gradient Fill </strong>are not functional.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><table class="relative-table wrapped" style="width: 74.0672%;"><colgroup><col style="width: 22.4322%;" /><col style="width: 25.7747%;" /><col style="width: 51.7722%;" /></colgroup><tbody><tr><th>Name</th><th>Value options</th><th>Description</th></tr><tr><th colspan="3"><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">Main</span></th></tr><tr><td>Use Gradient Fill</td><td>true/false</td><td><p>Specify whether a gradient should be used for the Fill Color and Content Fill Color <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Modifying styles of individual symbols" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[symbol style properties]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link>.</p></td></tr><tr><td>Show Line Jumps On</td><td>None<br />Horizontal Line<br />Vertical Line</td><td><p>Specify whether line jumps should be used for intersecting lines (e.g., paths).</p><ul><li data-uuid="6edae116-e9c1-49da-a0e6-164315e0e41c">None - line jumps are not used.</li><li data-uuid="f4637971-b8cc-4073-8fd1-8da36ed324fd">Horizontal Line - line jumps are used only on horizontal lines (default).</li><li data-uuid="91bc4dac-80a0-4813-bd32-609dff81d15b">Vertical Line - line jumps are used only on vertical lines.<br /><br /><br /></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="auto-cursor-target"><br /></p>
````

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=298090578 space=UAF2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 00213: Copy of Expose - su filtered import (neveikia)

- page_id: `298090578`
- space_key: `UAF2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UAF2P/pages/298090578/Copy+of+Expose+-+su+filtered+import+neveikia
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2025-02-25T18:13:37.434+01:00`
- ancestors: 
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

**On this page:**

A view usage exposes a portion of a model, specifying what model elements can be displayed by the view using the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Copy of Expose - su filtered import (neveikia)' space='UAF2P'] relationship. The exposed elements can be further specified using [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Copy of Expose - su filtered import (neveikia)' space='UAF2P']. Once the elements are exposed,the view [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Renderings' space='UAF2P'] can be applied to the exposed elements that meet all the view conditions to produce a [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Working with views' space='UAF2P'].

##### Element exposition kinds and visibility

Expose relationship is a kind of import relationship and is thus declared like an import relationship, but using the keyword *expose* instead of *import*. However, unlike imports, whose visibility can be modified, expose relationships always have *protected* visibility, which means that the elements exposed by a view usage are not publicly visible outside the view usage.

The exposition kind is specified as a specific suffix added to the exposed elements qualified name.

| Exposition kind | Suffix | Exposes | Excludes | Example |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Membership exposition | none | Only the specified namespace (i.e., element import). | The namespace's elements and their sub-namespaces (elements/packages). | part employeeInformation { part candidateData {} part employeeData { item employeeName; }}view 'Employee Information' {// membership exposition: expose employeeInformation; // exposes employeeInformation} |
| Namespace exposition | ::* | The content of the specified namespace. | The namespace itself.The namespace's sub-packages and their elements. Deeper nested sub-packages/elements can be accessed via name resolution.The sub-elements of the namespace's elements. Deeper nested sub-elements can be accessed via name resolution. | part employeeInformation { part candidateData {} part employeeData { item employeeName; }}view 'Employee Information' {// namespace exposition: expose employeeInformation::*; // exposes candidateData, employeeData} |
| Recursive membership exposition | ::** | The specified namespace and its content, including sub-namespaces and their elements. | Memberships inherited via implicit specializations. | part employeeInformation { part candidateData {} part employeeData { item employeeName; }}view 'Employee Information' {// recursive membership exposition: expose employeeInformation::**; // exposes employeeInformation, candidateData, employeeData, employeeName} |
| Recursive namespace exposition | ::*::** | The content of the specified namespace, including sub-namespaces and their elements. | The namespace itself.Memberships inherited via implicit specializations. | part employeeInformation { part candidateData {} part employeeData { item employeeName; }}view 'Employee Information' {// recursive namespace exposition: expose employeeInformation::*::**; // exposes candidateData, employeeData, employeeName} |

##### Element exposition

###### Exposing elements

To expose elements

1. In the Textual Editor, place the cursor within the body of the view element for which you want to expose the element(s).
2. Declare the keyword expose .
3. Specify the qualified name of the membership/namespace you want to import, followed by the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Copy of Expose - su filtered import (neveikia)' space='UAF2P'].
4. (Optional) [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Copy of Expose - su filtered import (neveikia)' space='UAF2P'] .
5. Click the Synchronize button.

partemployeeInformation{partcandidateData{}partemployeeData{itememployeeName;}}

view'Employee Information'{ 
expose employeeInformation::**; // recursive membershipexposition of *employeeInformation, candidateData, employeeData, employeeName*}

##### Element exposition filtering

Views have the capability to filter elements upon exposition based on certain conditions, usually defined in terms of the metadata provided by annotations of those elements. Only elements that meet all filter conditions are exposed for the view.

Ways to perform element exposition filtering:

- Filtered exposition combines filter conditions with the expose relationship itself by adding filter conditions in the *expose* declaration using square brackets [...] . For a filtered exposition, memberships are exposed from that specific exposition only if they satisfy all the given filter conditions.
  - It can be used for any namespace.
- Separately declared filter conditions are declared after the expose declaration, using the keyword filter .
  - Separately declared filter conditions can be used only for [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Package' space='UAF2P'] ([CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Importing and filtering elements' space='UAF2P']) and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='View' space='UAF2P'] (element exposition) elements.
- Defining a view by a view definition containing filtered exposition.

- Filter condition expression must be model-level evaluable. It can reference only literals, metadata annotations, and attributes, connected using basic arithmetic, comparison and Boolean operators.
- @ , istype , and hastype classification operators are commonly used to check if an element has the given metadata annotation.
- Element metaclass metadatas are located in used projects at Standard Libraries > SysML > Systems . You can either import the library or the needed element, or use a qualified name to target the specific element metaclass.
- Unlike separately declared filter conditions that require a qualified name for metadata-based filtering (e.g., *@MetadataDefinitions::Safety*), filtered exposition declaration can discard qualified names for metadata as long as all the needed namespaces are imported.

###### Filtered exposition

To filter exposition

1. In the Textual Editor, place square brackets at the end of the *expose* declaration you want to filter.
2. Within the square brackets, specify the filter condition expression, including the needed operator and the name of the element you want to expose.
3. Click the Synchronize button.

#### PANEL: Filtered exposition

Filtered exposition

packageMetadataDefinitions{

metadatadefSafety{attributeisMandatory:Boolean;}}

packageVehicle{ 
privateimportMetadataDefinitions::**; 
partvehicle{ 
partinterior{ 
partalarm; 
partseatBelt[2] { 
@Safety{isMandatory=true;} 
} 
partfrontSeat[2]; 
partdriverAirBag{ 
@Safety{isMandatory=false;} 
} 
} 
} 
}

// no need for qualified names for metadata when using filtered exposition declaration as long as all the needed namespaces are exposed 
 
view'Vehicle Features'{ 
// no need for qualified names for metadata when using filtered exposition declaration as long as all the needed namespaces are exposed: 
exposeSysML::Systems::**;// expose metaclass metadatas 
exposeMetadataDefinitions::**;// expose metadata definitions 
 
// you can use multiple filters in the exposition, but using separate brackets: 
exposeVehicle::**[@PartUsage][@SafetyandSafety::isMandatory];// exposes part usage elements from package *Vehicle*with *Safety* metadata attribute *isMandatory*value *true* 
}

###### Separately declared filter conditions

To specify separately declared filter conditions

1. In the Textual Editor, place the cursor within the body of the view containing an expose declaration.
2. Declare the keyword filter followed by filter condition expression, including the needed operator and the qualified name of the element you want to expose .
3. Click the Synchronize button.

#### PANEL: Separately declared filter conditions

Separately declared filter conditions

packageMetadataDefinitions{

metadatadefSafety{attributeisMandatory:Boolean;}}

packageVehicle{ 
privateimportMetadataDefinitions::**; 
partvehicle{ 
partinterior{ 
partalarm; 
partseatBelt[2] { 
@Safety{isMandatory=true;} 
} 
partfrontSeat[2]; 
partdriverAirBag{ 
@Safety{isMandatory=false;} 
} 
} 
} 
}

// separately declared filter conditions require a qualified name for metadata (e.g., 'MetadataDefinitions::Safety'), unlike filter import declaration

view'Vehicle Features'{ 
exposeVehicle::**;// exposes package *Vehicle*separately 
// you can use multiple filter condition declarations: 
filter@SysML::Systems::PartUsage;// exposes part usage elements from package *Vehicle* 
filter@MetadataDefinitions::SafetyandMetadataDefinitions::Safety::isMandatory;// exposes elements with *Safety* metadata attribute *isMandatory*value *true*from previously filtered part usage elements exposed from the package *Vehicle* 
}

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE
