/>}</span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></div></td></tr></tbody></table><h3>Element exposition</h3><h4>Exposing elements</h4><p><span style="color: rgb(68,71,70);">To expose elements</span></p><hr /><ol><li><span style="color: rgb(23,43,77);">In the Textual Editor, place the cursor within the body of the view element for which you want to expose the element(s).</span></li><li><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">Declare the keyword </span><em style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">expose</em><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">.</span></li><li>Specify the <span style="color: rgb(23,43,77);">qualified name of the membership/namespace you want to import, followed by the <ac:link ac:anchor="Element exposition kinds and visibility"><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[appropriate suffix for a recursive/membership/namespace exposition]]></ac:plain-text-link-body><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Copy of Expose - su filtered import (neveikia)" /></ac:link>.</span></li><li><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">(Optional) </span><ac:link ac:anchor="Element exposition filtering"><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Specify a filter for the exposition]]></ac:plain-text-link-body><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Copy of Expose - su filtered import (neveikia)" /></ac:link><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">. </span></li><li>Click the <strong>Synchronize<span> </span></strong>button.</li></ol><ac:structured-macro ac:name="panel" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="2dae463f-236c-45dd-9883-ecc7044ea2d8"><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">part</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> <span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">employeeInformation</span></span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> {<br /></span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">    </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">part</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">candidateData</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;"> {}<br /></span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">    </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">part</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">employeeData</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> {<br /></span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">        </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">item</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">employeeName</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">;<br /></span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">    }<br /></span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">}</span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">view</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">'Employee Information'</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> {</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">    </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">expose <span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">employeeInformation::**</span></span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">;   <span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);">// recursive membership </span></span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);">exposition of <em>employeeInformation, candidateData, employeeData, employeeName</em></span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"><br />}</span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="single"><ac:layout-cell><h3>Element exposition filtering</h3><p>Views have the capability to filter elements upon exposition based on certain conditions, usually defined in terms of the metadata provided by annotations of those elements. Only elements that meet all filter conditions are exposed for the view. </p><p>Ways to perform element exposition filtering:</p><ul><li><strong style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">Filtered exposition</strong><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;"> combines filter conditions with the expose relationship itself by adding filter conditions in the <em>expose</em> declaration using square brackets </span><em style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">[...]</em><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">. For a filtered exposition, memberships are exposed from that specific exposition only if they satisfy all the given filter conditions.</span><ul><li>It can be used for any namespace.</li></ul></li><li><strong>Separately declared filter conditions</strong> are declared after the <em>expose</em> declaration, using the keyword <em>filter</em>.<ul><li><span>Separately declared filter conditions can be used only for <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Package" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[package]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> (<ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Importing and filtering elements" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[element import]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link>) and <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="View" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[view]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> (element exposition) elements.<br /></span></li></ul></li><li style="color: rgb(255,0,0);"><span style="color: rgb(255,0,0);">Defining a view by a view definition containing filtered exposition.</span></li></ul><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="2e981b38-7a7e-4fd8-9868-448d2c5db34b"><ac:rich-text-body><ul><li>Filter condition expression must be model-level evaluable. It can reference only literals, metadata annotations, and attributes, connected using basic arithmetic, comparison and Boolean operators.</li><li><em>@</em>, <em>istype</em>, and <em>hastype</em> classification operators are commonly used to check if an element has the given metadata annotation.</li><li><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">Element metaclass metadatas are located in used projects at </span><em style="text-align: left;">Standard Libraries &gt; SysML &gt; Systems</em><em style="text-align: left;">. </em><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">You can either import the library or the needed element, or use a qualified name to target the specific element metaclass. </span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(23,43,77);">Unlike separately declared filter conditions that require a qualified name for metadata-based filtering (e.g., <em>@MetadataDefinitions::Safety</em>), </span>filtered exposition declaration can discard qualified names for metadata as long as all the needed namespaces are imported.</li></ul></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="two_equal"><ac:layout-cell><h4>Filtered exposition</h4><p>To filter exposition</p><hr /><ol><li><span style="color: rgb(23,43,77);">In the Textual Editor, place square brackets at the end of the <em>expose</em> declaration you want to filter.</span></li><li>Within the square brackets, specify the filter condition expression, including the needed operator and the name of the element you want to expose.</li><li>Click the <strong>Synchronize<span> </span></strong>button.</li></ol><ac:structured-macro ac:name="panel" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="a9e8499b-4a1a-4167-af80-da639ceb9515"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Filtered exposition</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">package</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">MetadataDefinitions</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> {</span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">    </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">metadata</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">def</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">Safety</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> {<br /></span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">        </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">attribute</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">isMandatory</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> : </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">Boolean</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">;<br /></span><span style="color: ## PAGE 00214: Copy of Import - su filtered import (neveikia)

- page_id: `298090581`
- space_key: `UAF2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UAF2P/pages/298090581/Copy+of+Import+-+su+filtered+import+neveikia
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2025-02-25T18:02:51.496+01:00`
- ancestors: 
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

**On this page:**

An import relationship allows one namespace to import memberships from another namespace. The member elements from imported memberships become (unowned) members of the importing namespace in addition to being members of the imported namespace. In particular, this allows members of the imported namespace to be referenced in textual notations within the scope of the importing namespace without having to qualify the member names with the name of the imported namespace.

##### Element import kinds and visibility

###### Import kinds

The import kind is specified as a specific suffix added to the import's qualified name.

| Import kind | Suffix | Imports | Excludes | Example |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Membership import | none | Only the specified namespace (i.e., element import). | The namespace's elements and their sub-namespaces (elements/packages). | package 'Employee Information' { part candidateData {} part employeeData { item employeeName; }}package 'Company Information' {// membership import: private import 'Employee Information'; // imports 'Employee Information'} |
| Namespace import | ::* | The content of the specified namespace. | The namespace itself.The namespace's sub-packages and their elements. Deeper nested sub-packages/elements can be accessed via name resolution.The sub-elements of the namespace's elements. Deeper nested sub-elements can be accessed via name resolution. | package 'Employee Information' { part candidateData {} part employeeData { item employeeName; }}package 'Company Information' {// namespace import: private import 'Employee Information'::*; // imports candidateData, employeeData} |
| Recursive membership import | ::** | The specified namespace and its content, including sub-namespaces and their elements. | Memberships inherited via implicit specializations. | package 'Employee Information' { part candidateData {} part employeeData { item employeeName; }}package 'Company Information' {// recursive membership import: private import 'Employee Information'::**; // imports 'Employee Information', candidateData, employeeData, employeeName} |
| Recursive namespace import | ::*::** | The content of the specified namespace, including sub-namespaces and their elements. | The namespace itself.Memberships inherited via implicit specializations. | package 'Employee Information' { part candidateData {} part employeeData { item employeeName; }}package 'Company Information' {// recursive namespace import: private import 'Employee Information'::*::**; // imports candidateData, employeeData, employeeName} |

###### Import visibility

The import visibility is specified as a specific keyword declared prior to the *import* keyword. The import visibility keywords are as follows:

- public - membership is visible outside the namespace.
- private - membership is invisible from outside the namespace.
- protected - membership is invisible outside the namespace, except in inheritance, where it behaves like public.

##### Element import

###### Importing elements

To import elements

1. In the Textual Editor, place the cursor where you want to import the element(s).
2. Specify the import [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Copy of Import - su filtered import (neveikia)' space='UAF2P'] , declaring the needed keyword.
3. Declare the keyword import .
4. Specify the qualified name of the membership/namespace you want to import, followed by the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Copy of Import - su filtered import (neveikia)' space='UAF2P'].
5. (Optional) [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Copy of Import - su filtered import (neveikia)' space='UAF2P'] .
6. Click the Synchronize button.

package'Employee Information'{ 
 part candidateData {} 
partemployeeData{ 
itememployeeName; 
} 
}

package'Company Information'{ 
privateimport'Employee Information'::**;// private recursive membership import of *'Employee Information'**, candidateData, employeeData, employeeName*}

###### Importing library elements

Import is especially useful for accessing library elements instead of using a qualified name each time.

#### PANEL: Qualified name instead of import

Qualified name instead of import

// instead of using a qualified name each time:

package'Employee Data'{ 
partemployeeData{ 
// accessing 'String' and 'Real' data types from the *ScalarValues* library via qualified name: 
itememployeeName:ScalarValues::String; 
itemID:ScalarValues::Real; 
} 
}

#### PANEL: Import instead of qualified name

Import instead of qualified name

// use import to access library elements:

package'Employee Data'{ 
private importScalarValues::**; // importing *ScalarValues* library 
partemployeeData{ 
itememployeeName:String; // no need for qualified name 
itemID:Real; // no need for qualified name 
} 
}

##### Element import filtering

Namespaces have the capability to filter elements upon import based on certain conditions, usually defined in terms of the metadata provided by annotations of those elements. Only elements that meet all filter conditions become imported members of the namespace.

There are two ways to perform element import filtering:

- Filtered import combines filter conditions with the import itself by adding filter conditions in the import declaration using square brackets [...] . For a filtered import, memberships are imported from that specific import only if they satisfy all the given filter conditions.
  - It can be used for any namespace.
- Separately declared filter conditions are declared after the import declaration, using the keyword filter .
  - Separately declared filter conditions can be used only for [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Package' space='UAF2P'] (element import) and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='View' space='UAF2P'] ([CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Filtering elements for views' space='UAF2P']) elements.

- Filter condition expression must be model-level evaluable. It can reference only literals, metadata annotations, and attributes, connected using basic arithmetic, comparison and Boolean operators.
- @ , istype , and hastype classification operators are commonly used to check if an element has the given metadata annotation.
- Element metaclass metadatas are located in used projects at Standard Libraries > SysML > Systems . You can either import the library or the needed element, or use a qualified name to target the specific element metaclass.
- Unlike separately declared filter conditions that require a qualified name for metadata-based filtering (e.g., *@MetadataDefinitions::Safety*), filtered import declaration can discard qualified names for metadata as long as all the needed namespaces are imported.

###### Filtered import

To filter import

1. In the Textual Editor, place square brackets at the end of the *import* declaration you want to filter.
2. Within the square brackets, specify the filter condition expression, including the needed operator and the name of the element you want to import.
3. Click the Synchronize button.

#### PANEL: Filtered import

Filtered import

packageMetadataDefinitions{metadatadefSafety{attributeisMandatory:Boolean;}}

packageVehicle{ 
privateimportMetadataDefinitions::**; 
partvehicle{ 
partinterior{ 
partalarm; 
partseatBelt[2] { 
@Safety{isMandatory=true;} 
} 
partfrontSeat[2]; 
partdriverAirBag{ 
@Safety{isMandatory=false;} 
} 
} 
} 
}

// no need for qualified names for metadata when using filtered import declaration as long as all the needed namespaces are imported

package'Vehicle Features'{ 
privateimportMetadataDefinitions::**;// import metadata definitionsprivateimportSysML::Systems::**;// import metaclass metadatas

// you can use multiple filters in the import, but using separate brackets:

privateimportVehicle::**[@PartUsage][@SafetyandSafety::isMandatory];// imports part usage elements from package *Vehicle*with *Safety*metadata attribute *isMandatory*value *true*

}

###### Separately declared filter conditions

To specify separately declared filter conditions

1. In the Textual Editor, place the cursor within the body of the package containing an import declaration.
2. Declare the keyword filter followed by filter condition expression, including the needed operator and the qualified name of the element you want to import .
3. Click the Synchronize button.

#### PANEL: Separately declared filter conditions

Separately declared filter conditions

packageMetadataDefinitions{metadatadefSafety{attributeisMandatory:Boolean;}}

packageVehicle{ 
privateimportMetadataDefinitions::**; 
partvehicle{ 
partinterior{ 
partalarm; 
partseatBelt[2] { 
@Safety{isMandatory=true;} 
} 
partfrontSeat[2]; 
partdriverAirBag{ 
@Safety{isMandatory=false;} 
} 
} 
} 
}

// separately declared filter conditions require a qualified name for metadata (e.g., 'MetadataDefinitions::Safety'), unlike filter import declaration

package'Vehicle Features'{ 
privateimportVehicle::**; // imports package *Vehicle* separately

// you can use multiple filter condition declarations:

filter@SysML::Systems::PartUsage;// imports part usage elements from package *Vehicle*

filter@MetadataDefinitions::SafetyandMetadataDefinitions::Safety::isMandatory;// imports elements with *Safety*metadata attribute *isMandatory*value *true*from previously filtered part usage elements imported from the package *Vehicle*}**

style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">item</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">ID</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> : </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">ScalarValues::Real</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">;</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">    }</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">}<br /></span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:layout-cell><ac:layout-cell><ac:structured-macro ac:name="panel" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="1eb6a049-d753-4d74-84ed-e805e9ca1c62"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Import instead of qualified name </ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);">// use import to access library elements:</span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">package</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> '<span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">Employee Data'</span></span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> {</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">    </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">private import</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">ScalarValues</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">::**;  <span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);">// importing <em>ScalarValues</em> library</span></span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">    </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">part</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">employeeData</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> {</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">        </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">item</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">employeeName</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> : </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">String</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">;   <span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);">// no need for qualified name</span></span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">        </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">item</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">ID</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> : </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">Real</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">;   <span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);">// no need for qualified name</span></span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">    }</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">}</span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="single"><ac:layout-cell><h3>Element import filtering</h3><p>Namespaces have the capability to filter elements upon import based on certain conditions, usually defined in terms of the metadata provided by annotations of those elements. Only elements that meet all filter conditions become imported members of the namespace. </p><p>There are two ways to perform element import filtering:</p><ul><li><strong style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">Filtered import</strong><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;"> combines filter conditions with the import itself by adding filter conditions in the import declaration using square brackets </span><em style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">[...]</em><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">. For a filtered import, memberships are imported from that specific import only if they satisfy all the given filter conditions.</span><ul><li>It can be used for any namespace.</li></ul></li><li><strong>Separately declared filter conditions</strong> are declared after the <em>import </em>declaration, using the keyword <em>filter</em>.<ul><li><span>Separately declared filter conditions can be used only for <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Package" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[package]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> (element import) and <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="View" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[view]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> (<ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="Filtering elements for views" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[element exposition]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link>) elements.<br /><br /></span></li></ul></li></ul><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="69834189-7a61-4af4-ac3a-db7ce99b7a9b"><ac:rich-text-body><ul><li>Filter condition expression must be model-level evaluable. It can reference only literals, metadata annotations, and attributes, connected using basic arithmetic, comparison and Boolean operators.</li><li><em>@</em>, <em>istype</em>, and <em>hastype</em> classification operators are commonly used to check if an element has the given metadata annotation.</li><li><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">Element metaclass metadatas are located in used projects at </span><em style="text-align: left;">Standard Libraries &gt; SysML &gt; Systems</em><em style="text-align: left;">. </em><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">You can either import the library or the needed element, or use a qualified name to target the specific element metaclass. </span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(23,43,77);">Unlike separately declared filter conditions that require a qualified name for metadata-based filtering (e.g., <em>@MetadataDefinitions::Safety</em>), </span>filtered import declaration can discard qualified names for metadata as long as all the needed namespaces are imported.</li></ul></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="two_equal"><ac:layout-cell><h4>Filtered import</h4><p>To filter import</p><hr /><ol><li><span style="color: rgb(23,43,77);">In the Textual Editor, place square brackets at the end of the <em>import</em> declaration you want to filter.</span></li><li>Within the square brackets, specify the filter condition expression, including the needed operator and the name of the element you want to import.</li><li>Click the <strong>Synchronize<span> </span></strong>button.</li></ol><ac:structured-macro ac:name="panel" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="62f34d46-99c4-420c-9b1a-4a5418912850"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Filtered import</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">package</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">MetadataDefinitions</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;"> {<br /></span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">    </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">metadata</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">def</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">Safety</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;"> {<br /></span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">        </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">attribute</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">isMandatory</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;"> : </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">Boolean</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">;<br /></span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">    }<br /></span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">}</span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">package<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">Vehicle</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> {</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">    </span>private<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span>import<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">MetadataDefinitions</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">::**;</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">    </span>part<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">vehicle</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> {</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">        </span>part<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">interior</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> {</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">            </span>part<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">alarm</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">;</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">            </span>part<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">seatBelt</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> [</span><span style="color: rgb(9,134,88);">2</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">] {</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">                @</span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">Safety</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">{</span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">isMandatory</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> = </span>true<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">;}</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">            }</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">            </span>part<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">frontSeat</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> [</span><span style="color: rgb(9,134,88);">2</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">];</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">            </span>part<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">driverAirBag</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> {</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">                @</span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">Safety</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">{</span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">isMandatory</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> = </span>false<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">;}</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">            }</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">        }</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">    }</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">}</span><br /></span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);"><span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);">// no need for qualified names for metadata when using filtered import declaration as long as all the needed namespaces are imported</span></span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">package<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">'Vehicle Features'</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> {</span><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">    </span>private<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span>import<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">MetadataDefinitions</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">::**;  </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);">// import metadata definitions<span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);"><br /><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">    </span>private<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span>import<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span></span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">SysML::Systems</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">::**;         <span> </span></span>// import metaclass metadatas<br /></span></span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);"><span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);">    // you can use multiple filters in the import, but using separate brackets:</span></span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">    </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">private</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">import</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">Vehicle</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">::**</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">[@ </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">PartUsage</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">]</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">[</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">@ </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);">Safety</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">and</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,17,136);">Safety::isMandatory</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">]; </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);">// imports <span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);">part usage elements from package <em>Vehicle </em></span>with <em>Safety </em>metadata attribute <em>isMandatory </em>value <em>true </em></span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);"><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">}</span></span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:layout-cell><ac:layout-cell><h4>Separately declared filter conditions</h4><p><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">To specify separately declared filter conditions </span></p><hr /><ol><li>In the Textual Editor, place the cursor within the body of the package containing an <em>import</em><em> </em>declaration.</li><li>Declare the keyword<span> </span><em>filter </em>followed by filter condition expression, including the needed operator and the qualified name of the element you want to import<span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">.</span></li><li>Click the <strong>Synchronize </strong>button.</li></ol><ac:structured-macro ac:name="panel" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="d35791f4-83c6-41f4-87e5-d3d23b9af69c"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Separately declared filter conditions</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">package</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;"> </span><span style="color: rgb(0,128,128);letter-spacing: 0.0px;">MetadataDefinitions</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);letter-spacing: 0.0px;"> {<br /></span><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;color: rgb(0,0,0);">    </span><span style="color: package <em>Vehicle</em></span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">    </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,255);">filter</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> @ </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">}</span><em><br /></em></span></span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section></ac:layout>
````

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=298090590 space=UAF2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 00215: COPY Predefined style sheets

- page_id: `298090590`
- space_key: `UAF2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UAF2P/pages/298090590/COPY+Predefined+style+sheets
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-03-26T12:07:24.077+01:00`
- ancestors: COPY Symbol styles
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

Each SysML v2 project is automatically loaded with the *3DS**SysML Customization* library that contains predefined style sheets comprised of sets of rules defining symbol styles based on element metaclass.The predefined style sheets are located in the *StyleSheets* package in the *<DS_Styles> DassaultSystemesStyles*namespace of the *3DS**SysML Customization* library.

There are two predefined style sheets in the *DS_Styles::StyleSheets*package:

50%

- DefaultStyleSheet The DefaultStyleSheet style sheet contains rule-based styles that apply to all element symbols in SysML v2 projects by default based on element metaclass.
  - You can view the predefined style definitions used for symbol styles in the 'Predefined style definitions' column in the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] page, and the DS_Styles::StyleSheets::ColorDefinitions package. [ATTACHMENT filename='defaultstylesheetpartdefinition.png']

50%

- BlackAndWhiteStyleSheet The BlackAndWhiteStyleSheet style sheet contains rule-based styles for representing all element symbols in black and white style. [ATTACHMENT filename='blackandwhitestylesheetpartdef.png']

You can:

- Use the default style sheet (default functionality).
- Switch between style sheets (predefined and/or custom ones). See the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] page.
- Create your own style sheets either by reusing and customizing an existing (predefined or custom) style sheet (e.g., DefaultStyleSheet ) or creating your own. See the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Custom style sheets' space='UAF2P'] and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] pages.

###### [IMAGE alt='' src=''] 
Symbol styles represented by the *DefaultStyleSheet*(left)**and *BlackAndWhiteStyle*Sheet**(right) style sheets.

##### Accessing predefined style sheets

To access the predefined style sheets

1. In the Containment tree, expand the following nodes: Used Projects > 3DS SysML Customization > DassaultSystemesStyles>StyleSheets .
2. Right-click the StyleSheets package and in the shortcut menu, click Open under Textual Editor . The style sheets' textual notation is opened in the Textual Editor.

##### *DefaultStyleSheet*style sheet components

The *DefaultStyleSheet*style sheet contains multiple rules for symbol styles conditioned by element metaclass. The styles applied to the rules use predefined style definitions. You can view them once you access the style sheet.

###### *DefaultStyleSheet*rules

The rules are structured with comments based on the element metaclass and look like the following:

/* -------------PART/PORT---------*/ 
partpartPortRule :> rule { 
part:>> condition : ByElementMetaclassCondition { 
refitem:>> elementMetaclass = (SysML::Systems::PartUsage.metadata, SysML::Systems::PartDefinition.metadata, SysML::Systems::PortUsage.metadata, 
SysML::Systems::PortDefinition.metadata); 
} 
view:>> style : AbstractGreenStyle; 
}

###### *DefaultStyleSheet*predefined style definitions

You can view the full list of predefined style definitions in the 'Predefined style definitions' column on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] page.

The predefined style definitions are listed in the *DS_Styles::StyleSheets::ColorDefinitions*packageand look like the following:

/* ------------------colors---------------------- */

viewdefAbstractGreenStyle:>ShapeStyle{ 
attribute:>>fillColordefault"#E3F2E3"; 
attribute:>>compartmentFillColordefault"#F6FBF6"; 
attribute:>>penColordefault"#123D15"; 
}

## PAGE 00216: COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables

- page_id: `298090622`

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

On this page, you can find the conditions and styles tables to use as a reference guide for the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Customizing style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] and/or [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] of rules for your style sheets.

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] . Contains [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Custom style sheets' space='UAF2P'] definitions, their ref items and value types.
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] . Contains [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Custom style sheets' space='UAF2P'] definitions, their attributes and value types, including primary style definitions and predefined style definitions.
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Style sheet conditions and styles tables' space='UAF2P'] . Contains [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Custom style sheets' space='UAF2P'] definitions, their attributes and value types, including primary compartment style definitions and predefined compartment style definitions

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=298090584 space=UAF2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 00217: COPY Symbol styles

- page_id: `298090584`
- space_key: `UAF2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UAF2P/pages/298090584/COPY+Symbol+styles
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-03-26T12:07:23.882+01:00`
- ancestors: 
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

Element symbols, including shapes and paths, are displayed on views based on the symbol styles defined in the style sheets in the *3DS SysML Customization*library that is loaded in every project. You can modify element symbol styles according to your preferences by working with style sheets.

Types of style sheet specification:

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Predefined style sheets' space='UAF2P'] Each SysML v2 project is automatically loaded with the*3DS SysML Customization* library that contains predefined style sheets comprised of sets of rules defining symbol styles based on element metaclass. The *DefaultStyleSheet*style sheet contains model-based styles that apply to all element symbols in SysML v2 projects by default based on element metaclass.
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Custom style sheets' space='UAF2P'] Instead of or in addition to using the existing style sheets, you can also create custom style sheets with your own sets of rules for symbol styles.
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Modifying styles of individual symbols' space='UAF2P'] Whether using a default or a custom style, y ou can customize the styles of individual symbols. Using the Symbol Style dialog, you can specify the style properties for specific symbols, determining their appearance. Changing the styles for an individual symbol via the Symbol Style dialog overwrites predefined and custom model-based symbol styles; the modifications persist even after updating [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] .
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Modifying styles of individual views' space='UAF2P'] Whether using a default or a custom style, y ou can customize the styles of individual views. Using the View Style dialog, you can specify the style properties for specific views, determining their appearance. Changing the styles for an individual view via the View Style dialog overwrites predefined and custom model-based symbol styles; the modifications persist even after updating [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] .

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### On the left: symbol styles using a predefined style sheet *DefaultStyleSheet*. 
In the middle: symbol styles using a predefined style sheet*DefaultStyleSheet*with the customized style for the individual attribute symbol. 
On the right: symbol styles using a custom style sheet.

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=298090618 space=UAF2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 00218: COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications

- page_id: `298090618`
- space_key: `UAF2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UAF2P/pages/298090618/COPY+Synchronizing+custom+style+sheet+modifications
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-03-26T12:07:25.564+01:00`
- ancestors: COPY Symbol styles > COPY Custom style sheets
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

Once you have created a style sheet and either customized the *DefaultStyleSheet* components or created custom ones, you need to synchronize the modifications in the Textual Editor and update all views for the modifications to be reflected in model views. Make sure to check whether you also need to assess layout-sensitive changes, as otherwise the updated styles will not be implemented.

##### Synchronizing modifications

Synchronization and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications' space='UAF2P'] do not affect customizations made to individual symbols via the **Symbol Style** dialog. See the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Modifying styles of individual symbols' space='UAF2P'] procedure on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Modifying styles of individual symbols' space='UAF2P'] page.

To synchronize modifications

1. Do one of the following:
  1. In the Textual Editor's toolbar, click the**Synchronize**button[IMAGE alt='' src=''].
  2. Use the Alt+S shortcut keys.
2. Ensure the new [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P'].
3. Press the **F5**key on the keyboard to update all affected views.
4. (Conditional) [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications' space='UAF2P']. You need to assess layout-sensitive changes if you already have views in your project and the style sheet contains updated values of the following attributes:General style attributes: *font*, *wrap, textVerticalPosition, textHorizontalPosition, lineStyle, orientation, isRounded, pathStyle, showPayload.*Compartment style attributes:*showCompartment, showShortName,showName, showFullText, showSpecialization, showQualifiedNameForSpecialization, showModifiers, showValue, showInheritedSign, showInherited, showOnlyOwned.*

##### Assessing layout-sensitive changes

Certain style attributes are layout-sensitive as changing their values can affect already-created views' layout. Whether you have [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Customizing style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] or [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Creating style sheet components' space='UAF2P'] and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='COPY Activating style sheets' space='UAF2P'] a new one if the updated style sheet contains styles with attribute values that are different from those that were used prior, you need to follow the procedure below to assess and either confirm or deny the changes.

Omitting this procedure means the modeling tool will not implement the updates of the new style and retain the previous attribute values representing symbols in the old style.

Follow the procedure below if you already have views in your project and the style sheet contains updated values of the following attributes:

- General style attributes: *font*, *wrap, textVerticalPosition, textHorizontalPosition, lineStyle, orientation, isRounded, pathStyle, showPayload.*
- Compartment style attributes: showCompartment, showShortName,showName, showFullText, showSpecialization, showQualifiedNameForSpecialization, showModifiers, showValue, showInheritedSign, showInherited, showOnlyOwned.

###### [IMAGE alt='' src='']The Symbol Style dialog displays the highlighted rows of the updated attributes after activating a new style sheet within which the values of layout-sensitive attributes are updated. 
At the top of the dialog, a notification provides commands for either using the new style or retaining the old one.

###### Assessing layout-sensitive changes

To assess layout-sensitive changes

1. In a view, right-click an affected symbol. The procedure must be performed for each affected symbol individually.
2. In the shortcut menu, click Symbol Style . The Symbol Style dialog opens.
3. Review the affected attributes in the highlighted rows. The rows display the old attribute values.
4. In the notification at the top of the dialog, click one of the following commands:
  1. Use the new style - implements the updated attribute values and displays the symbol in the new style.
  2. Retain the old style - does not implement the updated attribute values and displays the symbol in the old style. Undoing the commandTo undo the **Retain the old style** command for a selected attribute: 
If you retain the old style, the check boxes in the **Inherited**column are deselected because the affected attributes are not inherited from the current style sheet and are considered individually modified.You can undo the retained style and switch to the new one for the specific attribute by selecting the check box in the **Inherited**column for the appropriate attribute.To undo either the **Retain the old style**or**Use the new style**command for all attributes, do one of the following:Press **Ctrl+Z** on the keyboard.In the **main menu**, click **Edit**> **Undo**.
5. Click Close .

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

attributes:</span></span></p><ul><li><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);"><span>General style attributes: <em>font</em>, <em>wrap, textVerticalPosition, textHorizontalPosition, lineStyle, orientation, isRounded, pathStyle, showPayload.</em></span></span></li><li><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);"><span>Compartment style attributes: </span></span><em><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">showCompartment, showShortName, </span><span style="color:var(--ds-text-accent-blue-bolder,#09326c);">showName, showFullText, showSpecialization, showQualifiedNameForSpecialization, showModifiers, showValue, showInheritedSign, showInherited, showOnlyOwned.<br /></span></em></li></ul><h6 style="text-align: center;"><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="Assessing_layout_sensitive_changes.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UAF2P" ri:content-title="COPY Synchronizing custom style sheet modifications" /></ri:attachment></ac:image>The Symbol Style dialog displays the highlighted rows of the updated attributes after activating a new style sheet within which the values of layout-sensitive attributes are updated. <br />At the top of the dialog, a notification provides commands for either using the new style or retaining the old one.</h6><h4>Assessing layout-sensitive changes</h4><p>To assess layout-sensitive changes</p><hr /><ol><li>In a view, right-click an affected symbol.<br /><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="643cc83b-0e0a-4ac6-8787-818644a7392a"><ac:rich-text-body><p>The procedure must be performed for each affected symbol individually.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li><li>In the shortcut menu, click <strong>Symbol Style</strong>. The <strong>Symbol Style </strong>dialog opens.</li><li>Review the affected attributes in the highlighted rows. The rows display the old attribute values. </li><li>In the notification at the top of the dialog, click one of the following commands: <ol><li><strong>Use the new style</strong> - implements the updated attribute values and displays the symbol in the new style.</li><li><strong>Retain the old style</strong> - does not implement the updated attribute values and displays the symbol in the old style.<br /><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="aeb809d7-11d6-495c-a54b-9826072206b2"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Undoing the command</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><ul><li>To undo the <strong>Retain the old style</strong> command for a selected attribute:<br />If you retain the old style, the check boxes in the <strong>Inherited </strong>column are deselected because the affected attributes are not inherited from the current style sheet and are considered individually modified.<ul><li>You can undo the retained style and switch to the new one for the specific attribute by selecting the check box in the <strong>Inherited </strong>column for the appropriate attribute.</li></ul></li><li>To undo either the <strong>Retain the old style </strong>or<strong> Use the new style </strong>command for all attributes, do one of the following:<ul><li>Press <strong>Ctrl+Z</strong> on the keyboard.</li><li>In the <strong>main menu</strong>, click <strong>Edit </strong>&gt; <strong>Undo</strong>.</li></ul></li></ul></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li></ol></li><li>Click <strong>Close</strong>.</li></ol><p><br /></p>
````
